[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate[0m -- create, revoke, validate, bundle, and otherwise
      manage certificates

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate[0m [0;4;39mcommand[0m [0;4;39m[options][0m [0;4;39m[arguments][0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate[0m command group provides facilities for creating
      certificate signing requests (CSRs), creating self-signed certificates
      (e.g., for use as a root certificate authority), generating leaf or
      intermediate CA certificate by signing a CSR, validating certificates,
      renewing certificates, generating certificate bundles, and key-wrapping of
      private keys.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--help[0m, [0;1;99m-h[0m
          show help

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Create a root certificate and private key using the default parameters (EC
      P-256 curve):

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile root-ca

      Create a leaf certificate and private key using the default parameters (EC
      P-256 curve):

          $ step certificate create baz baz.crt baz.key --ca ./foo.crt --ca-key ./foo.key

      Create a CSR and private key using the default parameters (EC P-256
      curve):

          $ step certificate create zap zap.csr zap.key --csr

      Sign a CSR and generate a signed certificate:

          $ step certificate sign zap.csr foo.crt foo.key

      Inspect the contents of a certificate:

          $ step certificate inspect ./baz.crt

      Verify the signature of a certificate:

          $ step certificate verify ./baz.crt --roots ./foo.crt

      Lint the contents of a certificate to check for common errors and missing
      fields:

          $ step certificate lint ./baz.crt

      Bundle an end certificate with the issuing certificate:

          $ step certificate bundle ./baz.crt ./foo.crt bundle.crt

      Convert PEM format certificate to DER and write to disk.

          $ step certificate format foo.pem --out foo.der

      Extract the public key from a PEM encoded certificate:

          $ step certificate key foo.crt

      Install a root certificate in the system's default trust store:

          $ step certificate install root-ca.crt

      Uninstall a root certificate from the system's default trust store:

          $ step certificate uninstall root-ca.crt

[0;1;99mCOMMANDS[0m
      [0;1;99mbundle[0m         bundle a certificate with intermediate certificate(s) needed for certificate path validation  
      [0;1;99mcreate[0m         create a certificate or certificate signing request                                           
      [0;1;99mformat[0m         reformat certificate                                                                          
      [0;1;99minspect[0m        print certificate or CSR details in human readable format                                     
      [0;1;99mfingerprint[0m    print the fingerprint of a certificate                                                        
      [0;1;99mlint[0m           lint certificate details                                                                      
      [0;1;99mneeds-renewal[0m  Check if a certificate needs to be renewed                                                    
      [0;1;99msign[0m           sign a certificate signing request (CSR)                                                      
      [0;1;99mverify[0m         verify a certificate                                                                          
      [0;1;99mkey[0m            print public key embedded in a certificate                                                    
      [0;1;99minstall[0m        install a root certificate in the supported trust stores                                      
      [0;1;99muninstall[0m      uninstall a root certificate from the supported trust stores                                  
      [0;1;99mp12[0m            package a certificate and keys into a .p12 file                                               

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate bundle[0m -- bundle a certificate with intermediate
      certificate(s) needed for certificate path validation

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate bundle[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [0;4;39mca[0m [0;4;39mbundle-file[0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate bundle[0m bundles a certificate with any intermediates
      necessary to validate the certificate.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          The path to a leaf certificate to bundle with issuing certificate(s).

      [0;4;39mca[0m
          The path to the Certificate Authority issuing certificate.

      [0;4;39mbundle-file[0m
          The path to write the bundle.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Bundle a certificate with the intermediate certificate authority (issuer):

          $ step certificate bundle foo.crt intermediate-ca.crt foo-bundle.crt

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate create[0m -- create a certificate or certificate signing
      request

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate create[0m [0;4;39msubject[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
      [[0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m] [[0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m] [[0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m] [[0;1;99m--csr[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mprofile[0m] [[0;1;99m--template[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m] [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--san[0m=[0;4;39mSAN[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca[0m=[0;4;39missuer-cert[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-key[0m=[0;4;39missuer-key[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--bundle[0m] [[0;1;99m--skip-csr-signature[0m] [[0;1;99m--no-password[0m] [[0;1;99m--subtle[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--insecure[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate create[0m generates a certificate or a certificate
      signing request (CSR) that can be signed later using 'step certificate
      sign' (or some other tool) to produce a certificate.

      By default this command creates x.509 certificates or CSRs for use with
      TLS. If you need something else, you can customize the output using
      templates. See [0;1;99mTEMPLATES[0m below.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39msubject[0m
          The subject of the certificate. Typically this is a hostname for
          services or an email address for people.

      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          File to write CRT or CSR to (PEM format)

      [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
          File to write private key to (PEM format). This argument is optional
          if [0;1;99m--key[0m is passed.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkty[0m
          The [0;4;39mkty[0m to build the certificate upon. If unset, default is EC.

          [0;4;39mkty[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mEC[0m
              Create an [0;1;99melliptic curve[0m keypair

            [0;1;99mOKP[0m
              Create an octet key pair (for [0;1;99m"Ed25519"[0m curve)

            [0;1;99mRSA[0m
              Create an [0;1;99mRSA[0m keypair

      [0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m
          The [0;4;39msize[0m (in bits) of the key for RSA and oct key types. RSA keys
          require a minimum key size of 2048 bits. If unset, default is 2048 bits
          for RSA keys and 128 bits for oct keys.

      [0;1;99m--crv[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m, [0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m
          The elliptic [0;4;39mcurve[0m to use for EC and OKP key types. Corresponds to
          the [0;1;99m"crv"[0m JWK parameter. Valid curves are defined in JWA [RFC7518].
          If unset, default is P-256 for EC keys and Ed25519 for OKP keys.

          [0;4;39mcurve[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mP-256[0m
              NIST P-256 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-384[0m
              NIST P-384 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-521[0m
              NIST P-521 Curve

            [0;1;99mEd25519[0m
              Ed25519 Curve

      [0;1;99m--csr[0m
          Generate a certificate signing request (CSR) instead of a certificate.

      [0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mprofile[0m
          The certificate profile sets various certificate details such as
          certificate use and expiration. The default profile is 'leaf' which is
          suitable for a client or server using TLS.

          [0;4;39mprofile[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mleaf[0m
              Generate a leaf x.509 certificate suitable for use with TLS.

            [0;1;99mintermediate-ca[0m
              Generate a certificate that can be used to sign additional leaf certificates.

            [0;1;99mroot-ca[0m
              Generate a new self-signed root certificate suitable for use as a root CA.

            [0;1;99mself-signed[0m
              Generate a new self-signed leaf certificate suitable for use with TLS.
              This profile requires the [0;1;99m--subtle[0m flag because the use of self-signed leaf
              certificates is discouraged unless absolutely necessary.

      [0;1;99m--template[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate template [0;4;39mfile[0m, a JSON representation of the
          certificate to create.

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m set in the NotBefore property of the
          certificate. If a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339
          format. If a [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers,
          each with optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h"
          or "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m set in the NotAfter property of the certificate.
          If a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--san[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Add DNS or IP Address Subjective Alternative Names (SANs). Use the
          '--san' flag multiple times to configure multiple SANs.

      [0;1;99m--ca[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The certificate authority used to issue the new certificate (PEM
          file).

      [0;1;99m--ca-kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure the KMS used for signing the certificate

      [0;1;99m--ca-key[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The certificate authority private key used to sign the new certificate
          (PEM file).

      [0;1;99m--ca-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the CA
          private key.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m of the private key to use instead of creating a new one
          (PEM file).

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt the new
          private key or decrypt the user submitted private key.

      [0;1;99m--no-password[0m
          Do not ask for a password to encrypt the private key. Sensitive key
          material will be written to disk unencrypted. This is not recommended.
          Requires [0;1;99m--insecure[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--bundle[0m
          Bundle the new leaf certificate with the signing certificate. This
          flag requires the [0;1;99m--ca[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--skip-csr-signature[0m
          Skip creating and signing a CSR.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--subtle[0m
          Allow delicate operations.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mTEMPLATES[0m
      With templates, you can customize the generated certificate or CSR.
      Templates are JSON files representing a [0;1;39mcertificate[0m [1] or a
      [0;1;39mcertificate request[0m [2]. They use Golang's [0;1;39m[0;4;39mtext/template[0m[0m
      package [3] and [0;1;39m[0;4;39mSprig[0m[0m functions [4].

      Here's the default template used for generating a leaf certificate:

          {
            "subject": {{ toJson .Subject }},
            "sans": {{ toJson .SANs }},
          {{- if typeIs "*rsa.PublicKey" .Insecure.CR.PublicKey }}
            "keyUsage": ["keyEncipherment", "digitalSignature"],
          {{- else }}
            "keyUsage": ["digitalSignature"],
          {{- end }}
            "extKeyUsage": ["serverAuth", "clientAuth"]
          }

      And this is the default template for a CSR:

          {
            "subject": {{ toJson .Subject }},
            "sans": {{ toJson .SANs }}
          }

      In a custom template, you can change the [0;1;99msubject[0m, [0;1;99mdnsNames[0m,
      [0;1;99memailAddresses[0m, [0;1;99mipAddresses[0m, and [0;1;99muris[0m, and you can add custom
      x.509 [0;1;99mextensions[0m or set the [0;1;99msignatureAlgorithm[0m.

      For certificate templates, the common extensions [0;1;99mkeyUsage[0m,
      [0;1;99mextKeyUsage[0m, and [0;1;99mbasicConstraints[0m are also represented as JSON
      fields.

      Two variables are available in templates: [0;1;99m.Subject[0m contains the
      [0;4;39msubject[0m argument, and [0;1;99m.SANs[0m contains the SANs provided with the
      [0;1;99m--san[0m flag.

      Both .Subject and .SANs are objects, and they must be converted to JSON to
      be used in the template, you can do this using Sprig's [0;1;99mtoJson[0m function.
      On the .Subject object you can access the common name string using the
      template variable [0;1;99m.Subject.CommonName[0m. In [0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m below, you can
      see how these variables are used in a certificate request.

      For more information on the template properties and functions see:

          [1] https://pkg.go.dev/go.step.sm/crypto/x509util?tab=doc#Certificate
          [2] https://pkg.go.dev/go.step.sm/crypto/x509util?tab=doc#CertificateRequest
          [3] https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/
          [4] https://masterminds.github.io/sprig/

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Create a CSR and key:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.csr foo.key --csr

      Create a CSR using an existing private key:

          $ step certificate create --csr --key key.priv foo foo.csr

      Create a CSR using an existing encrypted private key:

          $ step certificate create --csr --key key.priv --password-file key.pass foo foo.csr

      Create a CSR and key with custom Subject Alternative Names:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.csr foo.key --csr \
            --san inter.smallstep.com --san 1.1.1.1 --san ca.smallstep.com

      Create a CSR and key - do not encrypt the key when writing to disk:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.csr foo.key --csr --no-password --insecure

      Create a root certificate and key:

          $ step certificate create root-ca root-ca.crt root-ca.key --profile root-ca

      Create an intermediate certificate and key:

          $ step certificate create intermediate-ca intermediate-ca.crt intermediate-ca.key \
            --profile intermediate-ca --ca ./root-ca.crt --ca-key ./root-ca.key

      Create a leaf certificate and key:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile leaf \
            --ca ./intermediate-ca.crt --ca-key ./intermediate-ca.key

      Create a leaf certificate and encrypt the private key:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile leaf \
             --password-file ./leaf.pass \
             --ca ./intermediate-ca.crt --ca-key ./intermediate-ca.key

      Create a leaf certificate and decrypt the CA private key:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile leaf \
             --ca ./intermediate-ca.crt --ca-key ./intermediate-ca.key --ca-password-file ./intermediate.pass

      Create a leaf certificate and key with custom Subject Alternative Names:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile leaf \
            --ca ./intermediate-ca.crt --ca-key ./intermediate-ca.key \
            --san inter.smallstep.com --san 1.1.1.1 --san ca.smallstep.com

      Create a leaf certificate and key with custom validity:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile leaf \
            --ca ./intermediate-ca.crt --ca-key ./intermediate-ca.key \
            --not-before 24h --not-after 2160h

      Create a self-signed leaf certificate and key:

          $ step certificate create self-signed-leaf.local leaf.crt leaf.key --profile self-signed --subtle

      Create a root certificate and key with underlying OKP Ed25519:

          $ step certificate create root-ca root-ca.crt root-ca.key --profile root-ca \
            --kty OKP --curve Ed25519

      Create an intermediate certificate and key with underlying EC P-256 key
      pair:

          $ step certificate create intermediate-ca intermediate-ca.crt intermediate-ca.key \
            --profile intermediate-ca --ca ./root-ca.crt --ca-key ./root-ca.key --kty EC --curve P-256

      Create a leaf certificate and key with underlying RSA 2048 key pair:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.crt foo.key --profile leaf \
            --ca ./intermediate-ca.crt --ca-key ./intermediate-ca.key --kty RSA --size 2048

      Create a CSR and key with underlying OKP Ed25519:

          $ step certificate create foo foo.csr foo.key --csr --kty OKP --curve Ed25519

      Create a root certificate using a custom template. The root certificate
      will have a path length constraint that allows at least 2 intermediates:

          $ cat root.tpl
          {
            "subject": {
              "commonName": "Acme Corporation Root CA"
            },
            "issuer": {
              "commonName": "Acme Corporation Root CA"
            },
            "keyUsage": ["certSign", "crlSign"],
            "basicConstraints": {
              "isCA": true,
              "maxPathLen": 2
            }
          }
          $ step certificate create --template root.tpl \
            "Acme Corporation Root CA" root_ca.crt root_ca_key

      Create an intermediate certificate using the previous root. By extending
      the maxPathLen we are enabling this intermediate sign leaf and intermediate
      certificates. We will also make the subject configurable using the
      [0;1;99m--set[0m and [0;1;99m--set-file[0m flags.

          $ cat intermediate.tpl
          {
            "subject": {
              "country": {{ toJson .Insecure.User.country }},
              "organization": {{ toJson .Insecure.User.organization }},
              "organizationalUnit": {{ toJson .Insecure.User.organizationUnit }},
              "commonName": {{toJson .Subject.CommonName }}
            },
            "keyUsage": ["certSign", "crlSign"],
            "basicConstraints": {
              "isCA": true,
              "maxPathLen": 1
            }
          }
          $ cat organization.json
          {
            "country": "US",
            "organization": "Acme Corporation",
            "organizationUnit": "HQ"
          }
          $ step certificate create --template intermediate.tpl \
            --ca root_ca.crt --ca-key root_ca_key \
            --set-file organization.json --set organizationUnit=Engineering \
            "Acme Corporation Intermediate CA" intermediate_ca.crt intermediate_ca_key

      Sign a new intermediate using the previous intermediate, now with path
      length 0 using the [0;1;99m--profile[0m flag:

          $ step certificate create --profile intermediate-ca \
            --ca intermediate_ca.crt --ca-key intermediate_ca_key \
            "Coyote Corporation" coyote_ca.crt coyote_ca_key

      Create a leaf certificate, that is the default profile and bundle it with
      the two intermediate certificates and validate it:

          $ step certificate create --ca coyote_ca.crt --ca-key coyote_ca_key \
            "coyote@acme.corp" leaf.crt coyote.key
          $ cat leaf.crt coyote_ca.crt intermediate_ca.crt > coyote.crt
          $ step certificate verify --roots root_ca.crt coyote.crt

      Create a certificate request using a template:

          $ cat csr.tpl
          {
              "subject": {
                  "country": "US",
                  "organization": "Coyote Corporation",
                  "commonName": "{{ .Subject.CommonName }}"
              },
            "sans": {{ toJson .SANs }}
          }
          $ step certificate create --csr --template csr.tpl --san coyote@acme.corp \
            "Wile E. Coyote" coyote.csr coyote.key

      Create a root certificate using [0;4;39mstep-kms-plugin[0m:

          $ step kms create \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            'pkcs11:id=4000;object=root-key'
          $ step certificate create \
            --profile root-ca \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            --key 'pkcs11:id=4000' \
            'KMS Root' root_ca.crt

      Create an intermediate certificate using [0;4;39mstep-kms-plugin[0m:

          $ step kms create \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            'pkcs11:id=4001;object=intermediate-key'
          $ step certificate create \
            --profile intermediate-ca \
            --ca-kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password'
            --ca root_ca.crt --ca-key 'pkcs11:id=4000' \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            --key 'pkcs11:id=4001' \
            'My KMS Intermediate' intermediate_ca.crt

      Create an intermediate certificate for an RSA decryption key in Google
      Cloud KMS, signed by a root stored on disk, using [0;4;39mstep-kms-plugin[0m:

          $ step certificate create \
            --profile intermediate-ca \
            --ca root_ca.crt --ca-key root_ca_key \
            --kms cloudkms: \
            --key 'projects/myProjectID/locations/global/keyRings/myKeyRing/cryptoKeys/myKey/cryptoKeyVersions/1' \
            --skip-csr-signature \
            'My RSA Intermediate' intermediate_rsa_ca.crt

      Create an intermediate certificate for an RSA signing key in Google Cloud
      KMS, signed by a root stored in an HSM, using [0;4;39mstep-kms-plugin[0m:

          $ step certificate create \
            --profile intermediate-ca \
            --ca-kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            --ca root_ca.crt --ca-key 'pkcs11:id=4000' \
            --kms cloudkms: \
            --key 'projects/myProjectID/locations/global/keyRings/myKeyRing/cryptoKeys/myKey/cryptoKeyVersions/1' \
            'My RSA Intermediate' intermediate_rsa_ca.crt

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate format[0m -- reformat certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate format[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate format[0m prints the certificate or CSR in a different
      format.

      Only 2 formats are currently supported; PEM and ASN.1 DER. This tool will
      convert a certificate or CSR in one format to the other.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          Path to a certificate or CSR file.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Path to write the reformatted result.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Convert PEM format to DER:

          $ step certificate format foo.pem

      Convert DER format to PEM:

          $ step certificate format foo.der

      Convert PEM format to DER and write to disk:

          $ step certificate format foo.pem --out foo.der

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate inspect[0m -- print certificate or CSR details in human
      readable format

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate inspect[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--bundle[0m] [[0;1;99m--short[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--format[0m=[0;4;39mformat[0m] [[0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroot-bundle[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mservername[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate inspect[0m prints the details of the certificate or CSR
      in a human- or machine-readable format. Beware: Local certificates are
      never verified. Always verify a certificate (using [0;1;99mstep certificate
      verify[0m) before relying on the output of this command.

      If crt-file contains multiple certificates (i.e., it is a certificate
      "bundle") the first certificate in the bundle will be output. Pass the
      --bundle option to print all certificates in the order in which they appear
      in the bundle.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          Path to a certificate or certificate signing request (CSR) to inspect.
          A hyphen ("-") indicates STDIN as [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--format[0m=[0;4;39mformat[0m
          The output format for printing the introspection details.

          [0;4;39mformat[0m is a string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mtext[0m
              Print output in unstructured text suitable for a human to read.

            [0;1;99mjson[0m
              Print output in JSON format.

            [0;1;99mpem[0m
              Print output in PEM format.

      [0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroots[0m
          Root certificate(s) that will be used to verify the authenticity of
          the remote server.

          [0;4;39mroots[0m is a case-sensitive string and may be one of:

            [0;1;99mfile[0m
              Relative or full path to a file. All certificates in the file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mlist of files[0m
              Comma-separated list of relative or full file paths. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mdirectory[0m
              Relative or full path to a directory. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file in the directory will be used for path validation.

      [0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          TLS Server Name Indication that should be sent to request a specific
          certificate from the server.

      [0;1;99m--bundle[0m
          Print all certificates in the order in which they appear in the
          bundle. If the output format is 'json' then output a list of
          certificates, even if the bundle only contains one certificate. This
          flag will result in an error if the input bundle includes any PEM that
          does not have type CERTIFICATE.

      [0;1;99m--short[0m
          Print the certificate or CSR details in shorter and more friendly
          format.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m
          Use an insecure client to retrieve a remote peer certificate. Useful
          for debugging invalid certificates remotely.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Inspect a local certificate (default to text format):

          $ step certificate inspect ./certificate.crt

      Inspect a local certificate bundle (default to text format):

          $ step certificate inspect ./certificate-bundle.crt --bundle

      Inspect a local certificate in json format:

          $ step certificate inspect ./certificate.crt --format json

      Inspect a local certificate bundle in json format:

          $ step certificate inspect ./certificate.crt --format json --bundle

      Inspect a remote certificate (using the default root certificate bundle to
      verify the server):

          $ step certificate inspect https://smallstep.com

      Inspect a remote certificate (using the standard port derived from the URL
      prefix):

          $ step certificate inspect smtps://smtp.gmail.com

      Inspect an invalid remote certificate:

          $ step certificate inspect --insecure https://expired.badssl.com

      Inspect a remote certificate chain (using the default root certificate
      bundle to verify the server):

          $ step certificate inspect https://google.com --bundle

      Inspect a remote certificate using a custom root certificate to verify the
      server:

          $ step certificate inspect https://smallstep.com --roots ./root-ca.crt

      Inspect a remote certificate using a custom list of root certificates to
      verify the server:

          $ step certificate inspect https://smallstep.com \
          --roots "./root-ca.crt,./root-ca2.crt,/root-ca3.crt"

      Inspect a remote certificate using a custom directory of root certificates
      to verify the server:

          $ step certificate inspect https://smallstep.com \
          --roots "./path/to/root/certificates/"

      Inspect a remote certificate chain in json format using a custom directory
      of root certificates to verify the server:

          $ step certificate inspect https://google.com --format json \
          --roots "./path/to/root/certificates/" --bundle

      Inspect a remote certificate chain in PEM format:

          $ step certificate inspect https://smallstep.com --format pem --bundle

      Inspect a local CSR in text format (default):

          $ step certificate inspect foo.csr

      Inspect a local CSR in json:

          $ step certificate inspect foo.csr --format json

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate fingerprint[0m -- print the fingerprint of a certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate fingerprint[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--bundle[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroot-bundle[0m] [[0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mservername[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--format[0m=[0;4;39mformat[0m] [[0;1;99m--sha1[0m] [[0;1;99m--insecure[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate fingerprint[0m reads a certificate and prints to STDOUT
      the certificate SHA256 of the raw certificate or certificate signing
      request.

      If [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m contains multiple certificates (i.e., it is a certificate
      "bundle") the fingerprint of the first certificate in the bundle will be
      printed. Pass the --bundle option to print all fingerprints in the order in
      which they appear in the bundle.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          A certificate PEM file, usually the root certificate.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroots[0m
          Root certificate(s) that will be used to verify the authenticity of
          the remote server.

          [0;4;39mroots[0m is a case-sensitive string and may be one of:

            [0;1;99mfile[0m
              Relative or full path to a file. All certificates in the file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mlist of files[0m
              Comma-separated list of relative or full file paths. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mdirectory[0m
              Relative or full path to a directory. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file in the directory will be used for path validation.

      [0;1;99m--bundle[0m
          Print all fingerprints in the order in which they appear in the
          bundle.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m
          Use an insecure client to retrieve a remote peer certificate. Useful
          for debugging invalid certificates remotely.

      [0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          TLS Server Name Indication that should be sent to request a specific
          certificate from the server.

      [0;1;99m--format[0m=[0;4;39mformat[0m
          The [0;4;39mformat[0m of the fingerprint, it must be "hex", "base64",
          "base64-url", "base64-raw", "base64-url-raw" or "emoji".

      [0;1;99m--sha1[0m
          Use the SHA-1 hash algorithm to hash the certificate. Requires
          [0;1;99m--insecure[0m flag.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Get the fingerprint for a root certificate:

          $ step certificate fingerprint /path/to/root_ca.crt
          0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3

      Get the fingerprint for a remote certificate:

          $ step certificate fingerprint https://smallstep.com
          e2c4f12edfc1816cc610755d32e6f45d5678ba21ecda1693bb5b246e3c48c03d

      Get the fingerprints for a remote certificate with its intermediate:

          $ step certificate fingerprint --bundle https://smallstep.com
          e2c4f12edfc1816cc610755d32e6f45d5678ba21ecda1693bb5b246e3c48c03d
          25847d668eb4f04fdd40b12b6b0740c567da7d024308eb6c2c96fe41d9de218d

      Get the fingerprint for a CSR using base64-url encoding without padding:

          $ step certificate fingerprint --format base64-url-raw hello.csr
          PJLNhtQoBE1yGN_ZKzr4Y2U5pyqIGiyyszkoz2raDOw

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate lint[0m -- lint certificate details

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate lint[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroot-bundle[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mservername[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate lint[0m checks a certificate for common errors and
      outputs the result in JSON format. It is intended for evaluating Web PKI
      certificates, and may not be appropriate for internal PKIs.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          Path to a certificate or certificate signing request (CSR) to lint.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroots[0m
          Root certificate(s) that will be used to verify the authenticity of
          the remote server.

          [0;4;39mroots[0m is a case-sensitive string and may be one of:

            [0;1;99mfile[0m
              Relative or full path to a file. All certificates in the file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mlist of files[0m
              Comma-separated list of relative or full file paths. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mdirectory[0m
              Relative or full path to a directory. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file in the directory will be used for path validation.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m
          Use an insecure client to retrieve a remote peer certificate. Useful
          for debugging invalid certificates remotely.

      [0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          TLS Server Name Indication that should be sent to request a specific
          certificate from the server.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
          $ step certificate lint ./certificate.crt

      Lint a remote certificate (using the default root certificate bundle to
      verify the server):

          $ step certificate lint https://smallstep.com

      Lint a remote certificate using a custom root certificate to verify the
      server:

          $ step certificate lint https://smallstep.com --roots ./certificate.crt

      Lint a remote certificate using a custom list of root certificates to
      verify the server:

          $ step certificate lint https://smallstep.com \
          --roots "./certificate.crt,./certificate2.crt,/certificate3.crt"

      Lint a remote certificate using a custom directory of root certificates to
      verify the server:

          $ step certificate lint https://smallstep.com --roots "./path/to/certificates/"

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate needs-renewal[0m -- Check if a certificate needs to be
      renewed

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate needs-renewal[0m [0;4;39mcert-file or hostname[0m
      [[0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mpercent|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--bundle[0m] [[0;1;99m--verbose[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroot-bundle[0m] [[0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mservername[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate needs-renewal[0m returns '0' if the certificate needs to
      be renewed based on its remaining lifetime. Returns '1' the certificate is
      within its validity lifetime bounds and does not need to be renewed. By
      default, a certificate "needs renewal" when it has passed 66% (default
      threshold) of its allotted lifetime. This threshold can be adjusted using
      the '--expires-in' flag. Additionally, by default only the leaf certificate
      will be checked by the command; to check each certificate in the chain use
      the '--bundle' flag.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcert-file or hostname[0m
          The path to a certificate OR a hostname with protocol prefix.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mpercent|duration[0m
          Check if the certificate expires within the given time window using
          [0;4;39mpercent|duration[0m. If using [0;4;39mpercent[0m, the input must be followed
          by a "%" character. If using [0;4;39mduration[0m, the input must be a sequence
          of decimal numbers, each with optional fraction and a unit suffix, such
          as "300ms", "-1.5h" or "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or
          "µs"), "ms", "s", "m", "h".

      [0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroots[0m
          Root certificate(s) that will be used to verify the authenticity of
          the remote server.

          [0;4;39mroots[0m is a case-sensitive string and may be one of:

            [0;1;99mfile[0m
              Relative or full path to a file. All certificates in the file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mlist of files[0m
              Comma-separated list of relative or full file paths. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mdirectory[0m
              Relative or full path to a directory. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file in the directory will be used for path validation.

      [0;1;99m--bundle[0m
          Check all certificates in the order in which they appear in the
          bundle.

      [0;1;99m--verbose[0m, [0;1;99m-v[0m
          Print human readable affirmation if certificate requires renewal.

      [0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          TLS Server Name Indication that should be sent to request a specific
          certificate from the server.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns '0' if the X509 certificate needs renewal, '1' if the
      X509 certificate does not need renewal, '2' if the X509 certificate file
      does not exist, and '255' for any other error.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Check if the leaf certificate in the file certificate.crt has passed 66
      percent of its validity period:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal ./certificate.crt

      Check if any certificate in the bundle has passed 66 percent of its
      validity period:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal ./certificate.crt --bundle

      Check if the leaf certificate provided by smallstep.com has passed 66
      percent of its vlaidity period:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal https://smallstep.com

      Check if any certificate in the bundle for smallstep.com has has passed 66
      percent of its validity period:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal https://smallstep.com --bundle

      Check if certificate.crt expires within 1 hour 15 minutes from now:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal ./certificate.crt --expires-in 1h15m

      Check if certificate for smallstep.com is expired or not:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal https://smallstep.com --expires-in 0s

      Check if certificate has passed 75 percent of its validity period:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal ./certificate.crt --expires-in 75%

      Check a remote certificate using a custom root certificate:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal https://smallstep.com --roots ./root-ca.crt

      Check a remote certificate using a custom list of root certificates:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal https://smallstep.com \
          --roots "./root-ca.crt,./root-ca2.crt,/root-ca3.crt"

      Check a remote certificate using a custom directory of root certificates:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal https://smallstep.com \
          --roots "./path/to/root/certificates/"

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate sign[0m -- sign a certificate signing request (CSR)

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate sign[0m [0;4;39mcsr-file[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
      [[0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mprofile[0m] [[0;1;99m--template[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m] [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--omit-cn-san[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--path-len[0m=[0;4;39mmaximum[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--bundle[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate sign[0m generates a signed certificate from a
      certificate signing request (CSR).

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcsr-file[0m
          The path to a certificate signing request (CSR) to be signed.

      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          The path to an issuing certificate.

      [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
          The path to a private key for signing the CSR.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mprofile[0m
          The certificate profile sets various certificate details such as
          certificate use and expiration. The default profile is 'leaf' which is
          suitable for a client or server using TLS.

          [0;4;39mprofile[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mleaf[0m
              Signs a leaf x.509 certificate suitable for use with TLS.

            [0;1;99mintermediate-ca[0m
              Signs a certificate that can be used to sign additional leaf certificates.

            [0;1;99mcsr[0m
              Signs a x.509 certificate without modifying the CSR.

      [0;1;99m--template[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate template [0;4;39mfile[0m, a JSON representation of the
          certificate to create.

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--omit-cn-san[0m
          Do not add CSR Common Name as SAN extension in resulting certificate.
          By default, the CSR Common Name will be added as a SAN extension only
          if the CSR does not contain any SANs. Note that if the Common Name is
          already captured as a SAN extension in the CSR then it will still
          appear as a SAN extension in the certificate.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt or decrypt
          the private key.

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m set in the NotBefore property of the
          certificate. If a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339
          format. If a [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers,
          each with optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h"
          or "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m set in the NotAfter property of the certificate.
          If a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--path-len[0m=[0;4;39mmaximum[0m
          The [0;4;39mmaximum[0m path length to set in the pathLenConstraint of an
          intermediate-ca. Defaults to 0. If it's set to -1 no path length limit
          is imposed.

      [0;1;99m--bundle[0m
          Bundle the new leaf certificate with the signing certificate.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Sign a certificate signing request using the leaf profile:

          $ step certificate sign leaf.csr issuer.crt issuer.key
          # or
          $ step certificate sign --profile leaf leaf.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR and bundle the new certificate with the issuer:

          $ step certificate sign --bundle leaf.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR with custom validity and bundle the new certificate with the
      issuer:

          $ step certificate sign --bundle --not-before -1m --not-after 16h leaf.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR but do not add the Common Name to the SANs extension of the
      certificate:

          $ step certificate sign --omit-cn-san leaf.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign an intermediate ca:

          $ step certificate sign --profile intermediate-ca intermediate.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign an intermediate ca that can sign other intermediates; in this
      example, the issuer must set the pathLenConstraint at least to 2 or without
      a limit:

          $ step certificate sign --profile intermediate-ca --path-len 1 intermediate.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR but only use information present in it, it doesn't add any key
      or extended key usages if they are not in the CSR.

          $ step certificate sign --profile csr test.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR with only clientAuth as key usage using a template:

          $ cat coyote.tpl
          {
            "subject": {
              "country": "US",
                  "organization": "Coyote Corporation",
                  "commonName": "{{ .Subject.CommonName }}"
            },
            "emailAddresses": {{ toJson .Insecure.CR.EmailAddresses }},
            "keyUsage": ["digitalSignature"],
            "extKeyUsage": ["clientAuth"]
          }
          $ step certificate create --csr coyote@acme.corp coyote.csr coyote.key
          $ step certificate sign --template coyote.tpl coyote.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR using a template and allow configuring the subject using the
      [0;1;99m--set[0m and [0;1;99m--set-file[0m flags.

          $ cat rocket.tpl
          {
            "subject": {
              "country": {{ toJson .Insecure.User.country }},
              "organization": {{ toJson .Insecure.User.organization }},
              "organizationalUnit": {{ toJson .Insecure.User.organizationUnit }},
              "commonName": {{toJson .Subject.CommonName }}
            },
            "sans": {{ toJson .SANs }},
          {{- if typeIs "*rsa.PublicKey" .Insecure.CR.PublicKey }}
            "keyUsage": ["keyEncipherment", "digitalSignature"],
          {{- else }}
            "keyUsage": ["digitalSignature"],
          {{- end }}
            "extKeyUsage": ["serverAuth", "clientAuth"]
          }
          $ cat organization.json
          {
            "country": "US",
            "organization": "Acme Corporation",
            "organizationUnit": "HQ"
          }
          $ step certificate create --csr rocket.acme.corp rocket.csr rocket.key
          $ step certificate sign --template rocket.tpl \
            --set-file organization.json --set organizationUnit=Engineering \
            rocket.csr issuer.crt issuer.key

      Sign a CSR using [0;4;39mstep-kms-plugin[0m:

          $ step certificate sign \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            leaf.csr issuer.crt 'pkcs11:id=4001'

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate verify[0m -- verify a certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate verify[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--host[0m=[0;4;39mhost[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroot-bundle[0m] [[0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mservername[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--issuing-ca[0m=[0;4;39mca-cert-file[0m] [[0;1;99m--verbose[0m] [[0;1;99m--verify-ocsp[0m]]
      [[0;1;99m--ocsp-endpoint[0m]=url [[0;1;99m--verify-crl[0m] [[0;1;99m--crl-endpoint[0m]=url

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate verify[0m executes the certificate path validation
      algorithm for x.509 certificates defined in RFC 5280. If the certificate is
      valid this command will return '0'. If validation fails, or if an error
      occurs, this command will produce a non-zero return value.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          The path to a certificate to validate.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--host[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Check whether the certificate is for the specified host.

      [0;1;99m--roots[0m=[0;4;39mroots[0m
          Root certificate(s) that will be used to verify the authenticity of
          the remote server.

          [0;4;39mroots[0m is a case-sensitive string and may be one of:

            [0;1;99mfile[0m
              Relative or full path to a file. All certificates in the file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mlist of files[0m
              Comma-separated list of relative or full file paths. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file will be used for path validation.

            [0;1;99mdirectory[0m
              Relative or full path to a directory. Every PEM encoded certificate from each file in the directory will be used for path validation.

      [0;1;99m--issuing-ca[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate issuer CA [0;4;39mfile[0m needed to communicate with OCSP and
          verify a CRL. By default the issuing CA will be taken from the cert
          Issuing Certificate URL extension.

      [0;1;99m--verify-ocsp[0m
          Verify the certificate against it's OCSP.

      [0;1;99m--ocsp-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The OCSP endpoint to use. If not provided step will attempt to check
          it against the certificate's OCSPServer AIA extension endpoints.

      [0;1;99m--verify-crl[0m
          Verify the certificate against it's CRL.

      [0;1;99m--crl-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The CRL endpoint to use. If not provided step will attempt to check it
          against the certificate's CRLDistributionPoints extension endpoints.

      [0;1;99m--verbose[0m, [0;1;99m-v[0m
          Print result of certificate verification to stdout on success

      [0;1;99m--servername[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          TLS Server Name Indication that should be sent to request a specific
          certificate from the server.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m
[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Verify a certificate using your operating system's default root
      certificate bundle:

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt

      Verify a remote certificate using your operating system's default root
      certificate bundle:

          $ step certificate verify https://smallstep.com

      Verify a certificate using a custom root certificate for path validation:

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt --roots ./root-certificate.crt

      Verify a certificate using a custom list of root certificates for path
      validation:

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt \
          --roots "./root-certificate.crt,./root-certificate2.crt,/root-certificate3.crt"

      Verify a certificate using a custom directory of root certificates for
      path validation:

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt --roots ./root-certificates/

      Verify a certificate including OCSP and CRL using CRL and OCSP defined in
      the certificate

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt --verify-crl --verify-ocsp

      Verify a certificate including OCSP and specifying an OCSP server

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt --verify-ocsp --ocsp-endpoint http://acme.com/ocsp

      Verify a certificate including CRL and specificing a CRL server and
      providing the issuing CA certificate

          $ step certificate verify ./certificate.crt --issuing-ca ./issuing_ca.pem  --verify-crl --crl-endpoint http://acme.com/crl

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate key[0m -- print public key embedded in a certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate key[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate key[0m prints the public key embedded in a certificate
      or a certificate signing request. If [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m is a certificate bundle,
      only the first block will be taken into account.

      The command will print a public or a decrypted private key if [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
      contains only a key.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          Path to a certificate or certificate signing request (CSR).

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m, [0;1;99m--output-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The destination [0;4;39mfile[0m of the public key.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Get the public key of a certificate:

          $ step certificate key certificate.crt
          -----BEGIN PUBLIC KEY-----
          MFkwEwYHKoZIzj0CAQYIKoZIzj0DAQcDQgAEio9DLyuglMxakS3w00DUKdGbeXXB
          2Mfg6tVofeXYan9RbvftZufiypIAVqGZqO7CR9EbkoyHb/7GcKQa5HZ9rA==
          -----END PUBLIC KEY-----

      Get the public key of a CSR and save it to a file:

          $ step certificate key certificate.csr --out key.pem

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate install[0m -- install a root certificate in the
      supported trust stores

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate install[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--prefix[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--all[0m] [[0;1;99m--java[0m] [[0;1;99m--firefox[0m] [[0;1;99m--no-system[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate install[0m installs a root certificate in the supported
      trust stores.

      Java's and Firefox's trust stores are also supported via the respective
      flags

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          Root certificate to install in the specified trust stores.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--prefix[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The prefix used to [0;4;39mname[0m the CA in the trust store. Defaults to the
          certificate common name.

      [0;1;99m--java[0m
          install on the Java key store

      [0;1;99m--firefox[0m
          install on the Firefox NSS security database

      [0;1;99m--no-system[0m
          disables the install on the system's default trust store

      [0;1;99m--all[0m
          install in Firefox's, Java's, and the system's default trust store

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Install a root certificate in the system's default trust store:

          $ step certificate install root-ca.pem

      Install a root certificate in all the supported trust stores:

          $ step certificate install --all root-ca.pem

      Install a root certificate in Firefox's and the system's default trust
      store:

          $ step certificate install --firefox root-ca.pem

      Install a root certificate in Java's and the system's default trust store:

          $ step certificate install --java root-ca.pem

      Install a root certificate in Firefox's and Java's trust store, but not in
      the system's default trust store:

          $ step certificate install --firefox --java --no-system root-ca.pem

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate uninstall[0m -- uninstall a root certificate from the
      supported trust stores

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate uninstall[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--prefix[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--all[0m] [[0;1;99m--java[0m] [[0;1;99m--firefox[0m] [[0;1;99m--no-system[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate uninstall[0m uninstalls a root certificate from the
      supported trust stores.

      Java's and Firefox's trust stores are also supported via the respective
      flags.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          Root certificate to uninstall from the specified trust stores.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--prefix[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The prefix used to [0;4;39mname[0m the CA in the trust store. Defaults to the
          certificate common name.

      [0;1;99m--java[0m
          uninstall from the Java key store

      [0;1;99m--firefox[0m
          uninstall from the Firefox NSS security database

      [0;1;99m--no-system[0m
          disables the uninstall from the system's default trust store

      [0;1;99m--all[0m
          uninstall from Firefox's, Java's, and the system's default trust store

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Uninstall only from the system's default trust store:

          $ step certificate uninstall root-ca.pem

      Uninstall a root certificate from all the supported trust stores:

      Uninstall a root certificate from Firefox's and the system's default trust
      store:

      Uninstall a root certificate from Java's and the system's default trust

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate p12[0m -- package a certificate and keys into a .p12
      file

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      step certificate p12 [0;4;39mp12-path[0m [[0;4;39mcrt-path[0m] [[0;4;39mkey-path[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--legacy[0m] [[0;1;99m--force[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--no-password[0m] [[0;1;99m--insecure[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep certificate p12[0m creates a .p12 (PFX / PKCS12) file containing
      certificates and keys. This can then be used to import into Windows /
      Firefox / Java applications.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--ca[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing a CA or intermediate certificate
          to add to the .p12 file. Use the '--ca' flag multiple times to add
          multiple CAs or intermediates.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt the .p12
          file.

      [0;1;99m--no-password[0m
          Do not ask for a password to encrypt a private key. Sensitive key
          material will be written to disk unencrypted. This is not recommended.
          Requires [0;1;99m--insecure[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--legacy[0m
          Encodes PKCS#12 files using the algorithms that were traditionally
          used, PBE+SHA1+RC2 for certificates and PBE+SHA1+3DES for keys.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns 0 on success and >0 if any error occurs.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Package a certificate and private key together:

          $ step certificate p12 foo.p12 foo.crt foo.key

      Package a certificate and private key together, and include an
      intermediate certificate:

          $ step certificate p12 foo.p12 foo.crt foo.key --ca intermediate.crt

      Package a CA certificate into a "trust store" for Java applications:

          $ step certificate p12 trust.p12 --ca ca.crt

      Package a certificate and private key with an empty password:

          $ step certificate p12 --no-password --insecure foo.p12 foo.crt foo.key

      Package a certificate and private key using a legacy encoder,

          $ step certificate p12 --legacy foo.p12 foo.crt foo.key

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
