[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep crypto[0m -- useful cryptographic plumbing

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep crypto[0m [0;4;39mcommand[0m [0;4;39m[options][0m [0;4;39m[arguments][0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      The [0;1;99mstep crypto[0m command group provides a selection of useful
      cryptographic primitives that balances completeness and safety
      (cryptographic strength, ease of use, and misuse prevention). Subcommands
      include flags and arguments to select algorithms and fine-tune behaviors,
      but we've selected safe defaults for you wherever possible.

      Insecure or subtle cryptographic primitives and options are gated with
      flags to prevent accidental misuse. Such primitives and options will not
      work unless you pass the corresponding flags to indicate that you
      understand the risks ([0;1;99m--insecure[0m and [0;1;99m--subtle[0m, respectively). Our
      rationale for these decisions is usually documented in the [0;1;99mSECURITY
      CONSIDERATIONS[0m section of the help for each subcommand.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--help[0m, [0;1;99m-h[0m
          show help

[0;1;99mSECURITY CONSIDERATIONS[0m
      The strength of cryptographic mechanisms depends on the strength of all
      links in the security chain. This includes the quality and strength of
      algorithms, random number generation, distribution mechanisms, etc. It also
      includes protection against hostile observation and tampering as well as
      the security of the overall system including the operating system and
      personnel, etc. Where possible, we've selected secure defaults. Whenever a
      subtle or insecure cryptographic operation is attempted affirmative
      confirmation via prompt or command line flag is required, indicating that
      you understand and accept the risks. That said, many of these factors are
      beyond the scope of this tool.

      [0;1;99mKey Length[0m
          This tool enforces a minimum key size of [0;1;99m256 bits for symmetric
          keys[0m, which is generally considered quantum-safe and accepted as
          sufficient for the foreseeable future.

          This tool enforces the NIST recommended minimum key size of [0;1;99m2048
          bits for RSA[0m keys, which RSA claims is equivalent in strength to 112
          bit symmetric keys and is likely to be sufficient until 2030. An RSA
          key length of at least 3072 bits, which RSA claims is equivalent to 128
          bit symmetric keys, should be used if security is required beyond 2030.

          Elliptic curve cryptography is generally believed to be secure with
          shorter keys than RSA requires. NIST guidelines state that ECC keys
          should be twice the length of the equivalent strength symmetric key.
          The rough equivalencies for the elliptic curves supported by this tool
          are:

          [0;1;99mkey type[0m  [0;1;99mcurve[0m  [0;1;99mRSA equivalent[0m  [0;1;99msymmetric key equivalent[0m  
          EC                     P-256               ~3000 bits                   ~128 bits                              
          EC                     P-384               ~4096 bits                   ~192 bits                              
          EC                     P-521               ~15000 bits                  ~256 bits                              
          OKP                    Ed25519             ~3000 bits                   ~140 bits                              

          Elliptic curve cryptography has the additional advantages of much
          smaller key sizes for equivalent security levels, and much faster
          cryptographic operations compared to RSA. The strength of these keys is
          generally considered sufficient for the predictable and foreseeable
          future.

          Note that for cryptographic protocols that have perfect forward
          secrecy and only use asymmetric keys for symmetric key negotiation your
          system will remain secure against future threats as long as the keys
          are large enough that they cannot be cracked today. In other words,
          sizing your keys to protect against potential future threats is largely
          irrelevant.

      [0;1;99mKey Use[0m
          In general you should not use an asymmetric keypair for both signing
          and encryption. Using a single key for both operations can introduce
          attack vectors that would not otherwise exist. Attacks aside, signing
          keys and encryption keys generally have different life cycles. Signing
          keys are generally destroyed once they're no longer useful for singing
          new data. Encryption keys, on the other hand, must be retained as long
          as data exists that was encrypted for the key. So using a signing key
          for encryption may force you to retain a signing key for longer than
          it's needed, leaving it susceptible to misuse.

          Raw public or private keys don't have any associated data, therefore
          this tool cannot enforce key use on raw keys and this responsibility is
          up to you. For keys in an "envelope" the envelope typically includes
          key use restrictions (e.g., the "use" parameter in JWKs and the "Key
          Usage" attribute of X.509 certificates). This tool generally requires
          key use to be specified when creating an enveloped key, and enforces
          key use restrictions when an enveloped key is being used.

      [0;1;99mSafe Curves[0m
          There is some concern that certain standard elliptic curves are very
          hard to implement correctly. These concerns are not purely theoretical.
          Implementation issues have been uncovered and real attacks have been
          demonstrated.

          While we take these concerns seriously, these curves are widely used
          in practice, largely because they are perceived to be stronger than RSA
          and have been implemented in more places than the "safe curves".
          Therefore, [0;1;99mwe've opted not to gate non-safe curves[0m. We've further
          elected to make [0;1;99mP-256[0m the default curve for EC keys.

          Still, it is important to be aware of the security risks associated
          with their risk. You should consider using "safe curves" if possible.
          We may change our mind as support for safe curves improves.

          Safe and non-safe curves implemented by this tool are:

          [0;1;99mkey type[0m  [0;1;99mcurve[0m  [0;1;99msafe[0m  
          EC                     P-256               NO                 
          EC                     P-384               NO                 
          EC                     P-521               NO                 
          OKP                    Ed25519             YES                

          For more information see [0;1;39mhttps://safecurves.cr.yp.to/[0m

      [0;1;99mQuantum Safety[0m
          Quantum-safe cryptography refers to keys and algorithms that are
          secure against an attack by a quantum computer. As of 2018 most public
          key algorithms are not quantum safe. In particular, [0;1;99mnone of the
          public key algorithms implemented by this tool are quantum safe[0m.
          However, no quantum computer exists that is powerful enough to break
          current algorithms. Using cryptographic protocols with forward secrecy
          is the best way to protect against future quantum attacks.

      [0;1;99mForward Secrecy[0m
          A cryptosystem or protocol has forward secrecy (or perfect forward
          secrecy) if, for each session or interaction, a random key is generated
          such that an attacker with access to all private keys would still not
          know the generated key. This can be accomplished using Diffie-Hellman
          key exchange, for instance.

          Forward secrecy can protect against an attacker who stores intercepted
          communication and waits for your private key to be compromised, at
          which point they could decrypt the stored communication. It also offers
          good protection against quantum attacks since symmetric key
          cryptosystems like AES are already considered quantum resistant with
          sufficiently large key sizes. The current best quantum attack against
          symmetric key systems requires work proportional to the square of the
          size of the key space. In other words, a symmetric key is half as
          strong against a quantum attack vs. a conventional attack, so your key
          needs to be twice as long for equivalent quantum-safe security. A 256
          bit symmetric key in the context of a quantum attack is equivalent in
          strength to a 128 bit key in the context of a conventional attack.

[0;1;99mCOMMANDS[0m
      [0;1;99mchange-pass[0m  change password of an encrypted private key (PEM or JWK format)    
      [0;1;99mkeypair[0m      generate a public / private keypair in PEM format                  
      [0;1;99mjwk[0m          create JWKs (JSON Web Keys) and manage JWK Key Sets                
      [0;1;99mjwt[0m          sign and verify data using JSON Web Tokens (JWT)                   
      [0;1;99mjwe[0m          encrypt and decrypt data and keys using JSON Web Encryption (JWE)  
      [0;1;99mjws[0m          sign and verify data using JSON Web Signature (JWS)                
      [0;1;99mjose[0m         collection of JOSE utilities                                       
      [0;1;99mhash[0m         generate and check hashes of files and directories                 
      [0;1;99mkdf[0m          key derivation functions for password hashing and verification     
      [0;1;99mkey[0m          manage keys                                                        
      [0;1;99mnacl[0m         easy-to-use high-speed tools for encryption and signing            
      [0;1;99motp[0m          generate and verify one-time passwords                             
      [0;1;99mrand[0m         generate random strings                                            
      [0;1;99mwinpe[0m        extract certificates and verify Windows Portable Executable files  

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep oauth[0m -- authorization and single sign-on using OAuth & OIDC

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep oauth[0m [[0;1;99m--provider[0m=[0;4;39mprovider[0m] [[0;1;99m--client-id[0m=[0;4;39mclient-id[0m
      [0;1;99m--client-secret[0m=[0;4;39mclient-secret[0m] [[0;1;99m--scope[0m=[0;4;39mscope[0m ...]
      [[0;1;99m--bare[0m [[0;1;99m--oidc[0m]] [[0;1;99m--header[0m [[0;1;99m--oidc[0m]]
      [[0;1;99m--prompt[0m=[0;4;39mprompt[0m] [[0;1;99m--auth-param[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m]

      [0;1;99mstep oauth[0m [0;1;99m--authorization-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mauthorization-endpoint[0m
      [0;1;99m--token-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mtoken-endpoint[0m [0;1;99m--client-id[0m=[0;4;39mclient-id[0m
      [0;1;99m--client-secret[0m=[0;4;39mclient-secret[0m [[0;1;99m--scope[0m=[0;4;39mscope[0m ...]
      [[0;1;99m--bare[0m [[0;1;99m--oidc[0m]] [[0;1;99m--header[0m [[0;1;99m--oidc[0m]]
      [[0;1;99m--prompt[0m=[0;4;39mprompt[0m] [[0;1;99m--auth-param[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m]

      [0;1;99mstep oauth[0m [[0;1;99m--account[0m=[0;4;39maccount[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--authorization-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mauthorization-endpoint[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--token-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mtoken-endpoint[0m] [[0;1;99m--scope[0m=[0;4;39mscope[0m ...]
      [[0;1;99m--bare[0m [[0;1;99m--oidc[0m]] [[0;1;99m--header[0m [[0;1;99m--oidc[0m]]
      [[0;1;99m--prompt[0m=[0;4;39mprompt[0m] [[0;1;99m--auth-param[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m]

      [0;1;99mstep oauth[0m [0;1;99m--account[0m=[0;4;39maccount[0m [0;1;99m--jwt[0m [[0;1;99m--scope[0m=[0;4;39mscope[0m
      ...] [[0;1;99m--header[0m] [[0;1;99m-bare[0m] [[0;1;99m--prompt[0m=[0;4;39mprompt[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--auth-param[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep oauth[0m command implements the OAuth 2.0 authorization flow.

      OAuth is an open standard for access delegation, commonly used as a way
      for Internet users to grant websites or applications access to their
      information on other websites but without giving them the passwords. This
      mechanism is used by companies such as Amazon, Google, Facebook, Microsoft
      and Twitter to permit the users to share information about their accounts
      with third party applications or websites. Learn more at
      [0;1;39mhttps://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OAuth[0m.

      This command by default performs the authorization flow with a
      preconfigured Google application, but a custom one can be set combining the
      flags [0;1;99m--client-id[0m, [0;1;99m--client-secret[0m, and [0;1;99m--provider[0m. The
      provider value must be set to the OIDC discovery document
      (.well-known/openid-configuration) endpoint. If Google is used this flag is
      not necessary, but the appropriate value would be be
      [0;1;39mhttps://accounts.google.com[0m or
      [0;1;39mhttps://accounts.google.com/.well-known/openid-configuration[0m

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--provider[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m, [0;1;99m--idp[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth provider for authentication

      [0;1;99m--email[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m, [0;1;99m-e[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Email to authenticate

      [0;1;99m--console[0m, [0;1;99m-c[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining only inside the terminal. This flag
          defaults to use the Device Authorization Grant flow.

      [0;1;99m--console-flow[0m=[0;4;39mflow[0m
          The alternative OAuth [0;4;39mflow[0m to use for input constrained devices.

          [0;4;39mconsole-flow[0m is a case-insensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mdevice[0m
              Use the Device Authorization Grant ([0;1;39mhttps://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8628#section-3.2[0m) flow

            [0;1;99moob[0m
              Use the Out of Band (OOB) flow

      [0;1;99m--client-id[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth Client ID

      [0;1;99m--client-secret[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth Client Secret

      [0;1;99m--account[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          JSON file containing account details

      [0;1;99m--authorization-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth Authorization Endpoint

      [0;1;99m--device-authorization-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth Device Authorization Endpoint

      [0;1;99m--token-endpoint[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth Token Endpoint

      [0;1;99m--header[0m
          Output HTTP Authorization Header (suitable for use with curl)

      [0;1;99m--oidc[0m
          Output OIDC Token instead of OAuth Access Token

      [0;1;99m--bare[0m
          Only output the token

      [0;1;99m--scope[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth scopes

      [0;1;99m--auth-param[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          OAuth additional authentication parameters to include as part of the
          URL query. Use this flag multiple times to add multiple parameters.
          This flag expects a 'key' and 'value' in the format '--auth-param
          "key=value"'.

      [0;1;99m--prompt[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Whether the Authorization Server prompts the End-User for
          reauthentication and consent. OpenID standard defines the following
          values, but your provider may support some or none of them:

            [0;1;99mnone[0m
              The Authorization Server MUST NOT display any authentication or consent user interface pages.
              An error is returned if an End-User is not already authenticated or the Client does not have
              pre-configured consent for the requested Claims or does not fulfill other conditions for
              processing the request.

            [0;1;99mlogin[0m
              The Authorization Server SHOULD prompt the End-User for reauthentication. If it cannot
              reauthenticate the End-User, it MUST return an error, typically login_required.

            [0;1;99mconsent[0m
              The Authorization Server SHOULD prompt the End-User for consent before returning information
              to the Client. If it cannot obtain consent, it MUST return an error, typically consent_required.

            [0;1;99mselect_account[0m
              The Authorization Server SHOULD prompt the End-User to select a user account. This enables an
              End-User who has multiple accounts at the Authorization Server to select amongst the multiple
              accounts that they might have current sessions for. If it cannot obtain an account selection
              choice made by the End-User, it MUST return an error, typically account_selection_required.

      [0;1;99m--jwt[0m
          Generate a JWT Auth token instead of an OAuth Token (only works with
          service accounts)

      [0;1;99m--listen[0m=[0;4;39maddress[0m
          Callback listener [0;4;39maddress[0m (e.g. ":10000")

      [0;1;99m--listen-url[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          The redirect_uri [0;4;39murl[0m in the authorize request (e.g.
          "[0;1;39mhttp://127.0.0.1:10000"[0m)

      [0;1;99m--redirect-url[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          The [0;4;39murl[0m to open in the system browser when the OAuth flow is
          successful.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Do the OAuth 2.0 flow using the default client:

          $ step oauth

      Redirect to localhost instead of 127.0.0.1:

          $ step oauth --listen localhost:0

      Redirect to a fixed port instead of random one:

          $ step oauth --listen :10000

      Redirect to a fixed url but listen on all the interfaces:

          $ step oauth --listen 0.0.0.0:10000 --listen-url http://127.0.0.1:10000

      Get just the access token:

          $ step oauth --bare

      Get just the OIDC token:

          $ step oauth --oidc --bare

      Use a custom OAuth2.0 server:

          $ step oauth --client-id my-client-id --client-secret my-client-secret \
            --provider https://example.org

      Use the Device Authorization Grant flow for input constrained clients:

          $ step oauth --client-id my-client-id --client-secret my-client-secret --console-flow device

      Use the Out Of Band flow for input constrained clients:

          $ step oauth --client-id my-client-id --client-secret my-client-secret --console-flow oob

      Use the default OAuth flow for input constrained clients:

          $ step oauth --client-id my-client-id --client-secret my-client-secret --console

      Use additional authentication parameters:

          $ step oauth --client-id my-client-id --client-secret my-client-secret \
            --provider https://example.org --auth-param "access_type=offline"

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca[0m -- initialize and manage a certificate authority

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca[0m [0;4;39mcommand[0m [0;4;39m[options][0m [0;4;39m[arguments][0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca[0m command group provides facilities to initialize a certificate
      authority, retrieve the root of trust, sign and renew certificates, and
      create and manage provisioners.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--help[0m, [0;1;99m-h[0m
          show help

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Create the configuration for a new certificate authority:

          $ step ca init

      Configure the ca-url and root in the environment:

          $ step ca bootstrap \
            --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com \
            --fingerprint 0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3
          $ cat $STEPPATH/config/defaults.json
          {
            "ca-url": "https://ca.smallstep.com",
            "fingerprint": "0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3",
            "root": "/home/user/.step/certs/root_ca.crt"
          }

      Download the root_ca.crt:

          $ step ca root root_ca.crt \
            --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com \
            --fingerprint 0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3

      Get the Health status of the CA:

          $ step ca health --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com --root /home/user/.step/certs/root_ca.crt

      Create a new certificate using a token:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token internal.example.com)
          $ step ca certificate internal.example.com internal.crt internal.key \
            --token $TOKEN --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com --root root_ca.crt

      Renew a certificate (certificate must still be valid):

          $ step ca renew internal.crt internal.key \
            --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com --root root_ca.crt

[0;1;99mCOMMANDS[0m
      [0;1;99mhealth[0m       get the status of the CA                                                   
      [0;1;99minit[0m         initialize the CA PKI                                                      
      [0;1;99mbootstrap[0m    initialize the environment to use the CA commands                          
      [0;1;99mtoken[0m        generate an OTT granting access to the CA

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca health[0m -- get the status of the CA

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca health[0m [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca health[0m makes an API request to the /health endpoint of the
      Step CA to check if it is running. If the CA is healthy, the response will
      be 'ok'.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Using the required flags:

          $ step ca health --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com:8080 --root path/to/root_ca.crt
          ok

      With the required flags preconfigured:

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m is set using environment variables (as STEP_CA_URL) or the
      default configuration file in [0;4;39m$STEPPATH/config/defaults.json[0m.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m is set using environment variables (as STEP_ROOT), the default
      configuration file in [0;4;39m$STEPPATH/config/defaults.json[0m or the default
      root certificate located in [0;4;39m$STEPPATH/certs/root_ca.crt[0m

          $ step ca health
          ok

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m -- initialize the CA PKI

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--key-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--pki[0m] [[0;1;99m--ssh[0m] [[0;1;99m--helm[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--deployment-type[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--name[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--dns[0m=[0;4;39mdns[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--address[0m=[0;4;39maddress[0m] [[0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--admin-subject[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m] [[0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ra[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m] [[0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--with-ca-url[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m] [[0;1;99m--no-db[0m] [[0;1;99m--remote-management[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--acme[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m command initializes a public key infrastructure (PKI) to
      be used by the Certificate Authority.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path of an existing PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m to be used as the root
          certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path of an existing key [0;4;39mfile[0m of the root certificate
          authority.

      [0;1;99m--key-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          existing root certificate key.

      [0;1;99m--pki[0m
          Generate only the PKI without the CA configuration.

      [0;1;99m--ssh[0m
          Create keys to sign SSH certificates.

      [0;1;99m--helm[0m
          Generates a Helm values YAML to be used with step-certificates chart.

      [0;1;99m--deployment-type[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m of the deployment type to use. Options are:

            [0;1;99mstandalone[0m
              An instance of step-ca that does not connect to any cloud services. You
              manage authority keys and configuration yourself.
              Choose standalone if you'd like to run step-ca yourself and do not want
              cloud services or commercial support.

            [0;1;99mlinked[0m
              An instance of step-ca with locally managed keys that connects to your
              Certificate Manager account for provisioner management, alerting,
              reporting, revocation, and other managed services.
              Choose linked if you'd like cloud services and support, but need to
              control your authority's signing keys.

            [0;1;99mhosted[0m
              A highly available, fully-managed instance of step-ca run by smallstep
              just for you.
              Choose hosted if you'd like cloud services and support.

          More information and pricing at: [0;1;39mhttps://u.step.sm/cm[0m

      [0;1;99m--name[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m of the new PKI.

      [0;1;99m--dns[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The DNS [0;4;39mname[0m or IP address of the new CA. Use the '--dns' flag
          multiple times to configure multiple DNS names.

      [0;1;99m--address[0m=[0;4;39maddress[0m
          The [0;4;39maddress[0m that the new CA will listen at.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m of the first provisioner.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt the keys.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt the
          provisioner key.

      [0;1;99m--with-ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the Step Certificate Authority to write in defaults.json

      [0;1;99m--ra[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m
          The registration authority [0;4;39mtype[0m to use. Currently "StepCAS" and
          "CloudCAS" are supported.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m
          The key manager service [0;4;39mtype[0m to use to manage keys. Options are:

            [0;1;99mazurekms[0m
              Use Azure Key Vault to manage X.509 and SSH keys. The key URIs have
              the following format [0;4;39mazurekms:name=key-name;vault=vault-name[0m.

      [0;1;99m--kms-root[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          The kms [0;4;39mURI[0m used to generate the root certificate key. Examples
          are:

            [0;1;99mazurekms[0m
              azurekms:name=my-root-key;vault=my-vault

      [0;1;99m--kms-intermediate[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          The kms [0;4;39mURI[0m used to generate the intermediate certificate key.
          Examples are:

            [0;1;99mazurekms[0m
              azurekms:name=my-intermediate-key;vault=my-vault

      [0;1;99m--kms-ssh-host[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          The kms [0;4;39mURI[0m used to generate the key used to sign SSH host
          certificates. Examples are:

            [0;1;99mazurekms[0m
              azurekms:name=my-host-key;vault=my-vault

      [0;1;99m--kms-ssh-user[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          The kms [0;4;39mURI[0m used to generate the key used to sign SSH user
          certificates. Examples are:

            [0;1;99mazurekms[0m
              azurekms:name=my-user-key;vault=my-vault

      [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          The registration authority issuer [0;4;39murl[0m to use.

          If StepCAS is used, this flag should be the URL of the CA to connect
          to, e.g [0;1;39mhttps://ca.smallstep.com:9000[0m

          If CloudCAS is used, this flag should be the resource name of the
          intermediate certificate to use. This has the format
          'projects/*/locations/*/caPools/*/certificateAuthorities/*'.

      [0;1;99m--issuer-fingerprint[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m
          The root certificate [0;4;39mfingerprint[0m of the issuer CA. This flag is
          supported in "StepCAS", and it should be the result of running:

              $ step certificate fingerprint root_ca.crt
              4fe5f5ef09e95c803fdcb80b8cf511e2a885eb86f3ce74e3e90e62fa3faf1531

      [0;1;99m--issuer-provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m of an existing provisioner in the issuer CA. This flag is
          supported in "StepCAS".

      [0;1;99m--credentials-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The registration authority credentials [0;4;39mfile[0m to use.

          If CloudCAS is used, this flag should be the path to a service account
          key. It can also be set using the 'GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS=path'
          environment variable or the default service account in an instance in
          Google Cloud.

      [0;1;99m--no-db[0m
          Generate a CA configuration without the DB stanza. No persistence
          layer.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m of the context for the new authority.

      [0;1;99m--remote-management[0m
          Enable Remote Management. Defaults to false.

      [0;1;99m--acme[0m
          Create a default ACME provisioner. Defaults to false.

      [0;1;99m--admin-subject[0m=[0;4;39msubject[0m, [0;1;99m--admin-name[0m=[0;4;39msubject[0m
          The admin [0;4;39msubject[0m to use for generating admin credentials.

      [0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m that will serve as the profile name for the context.

      [0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m that will serve as the authority name for the context.

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca bootstrap[0m -- initialize the environment to use the CA commands

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca bootstrap[0m [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--fingerprint[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m] [[0;1;99m--install[0m] [[0;1;99m--team[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--team-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--redirect-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--team-authority[0m=[0;4;39msub-domain[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca bootstrap[0m downloads the root certificate from the certificate
      authority and sets up the current environment to use it.

      Bootstrap will store the root certificate in
      [0;4;39m$STEPPATH/certs/root_ca.crt[0m and create a configuration file in
      [0;4;39m$STEPPATH/configs/defaults.json[0m with the CA url, the root certificate
      location and its fingerprint.

      After the bootstrap, ca commands do not need to specify the flags
      --ca-url, --root or --fingerprint if we want to use the same environment.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--fingerprint[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m
          The [0;4;39mfingerprint[0m of the targeted root certificate.

      [0;1;99m--install[0m
          Install the root certificate into the system's default trust store.

      [0;1;99m--team[0m=[0;4;39mID[0m
          The team [0;4;39mID[0m used to bootstrap the environment.

      [0;1;99m--team-authority[0m=[0;4;39msub-domain[0m
          The [0;4;39msub-domain[0m of the certificate authority to bootstrap. E.g.,
          for an authority with domain name 'certs.example-team.ca.smallstep.com'
          the value would be 'certs'.

      [0;1;99m--team-url[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          The [0;4;39murl[0m step queries to retrieve initial team configuration. Only
          used with the [0;1;99m--team[0m option. If the url contains [0;4;39m<>[0m
          placeholders, they are replaced with the team ID. Replacing the
          authority-id section of the url is not supported with placeholders.

      [0;1;99m--redirect-url[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          The [0;4;39murl[0m to open in the system browser when the OAuth flow is
          successful.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

      [0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m that will serve as the profile name for the context.

      [0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m that will serve as the authority name for the context.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Bootstrap using the CA url and a fingerprint:

          $ step ca bootstrap --ca-url https://ca.example.com \
            --fingerprint d9d0978692f1c7cc791f5c343ce98771900721405e834cd27b9502cc719f5097

      Bootstrap and install the root certificate

          $ step ca bootstrap --ca-url https://ca.example.com \
            --fingerprint d9d0978692f1c7cc791f5c343ce98771900721405e834cd27b9502cc719f5097 \
            --install

      Bootstrap with a smallstep.com CA using a team ID:

          $ step ca bootstrap --team superteam

      To use team IDs in your own environment, you'll need an HTTP(S) server
      serving a JSON file:

          {"url":"https://ca.example.com","fingerprint":"d9d0978692f1c7cc791f5c343ce98771900721405e834cd27b9502cc719f5097"}

      Then, this command will look for the file at
      [0;1;39mhttps://config.example.com/superteam:[0m

          $ step ca bootstrap --team superteam --team-url https://config.example.com/<>

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca token[0m -- generate an OTT granting access to the CA

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca token[0m [0;4;39msubject[0m [--[0;1;99mkid[0m=[0;4;39mkid[0m] [--[0;1;99missuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--cert-not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--cert-not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--output-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--kms[0m=uri] [[0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--san[0m=[0;4;39mSAN[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--revoke[0m] [[0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--x5c-insecure[0m] [[0;1;99m--sshpop-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--sshpop-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--cnf[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m] [[0;1;99m--cnf-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ssh[0m] [[0;1;99m--host[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--principal[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m] [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca token[0m command generates a one-time token granting access to
      the certificates authority.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39msubject[0m
          The Common Name, DNS Name, or IP address that will be set by the
          certificate authority. When there are no additional Subject Alternative
          Names configured (via the --san flag), the subject will be added as the
          only element of the 'sans' claim on the token.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--kid[0m=[0;4;39mkid[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mkid[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--san[0m=[0;4;39mdns|ip|email|uri[0m
          Add [0;4;39mdns|ip|email|uri[0m Subject Alternative Name(s) (SANs) that
          should be authorized. A certificate signing request using this token
          must match the complete set of SANs in the token 1:1. Use the '--san'
          flag multiple times to configure multiple SANs.

      [0;1;99m--principal[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m-n[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          Add the principals (user or host [0;4;39mname[0ms) that the token is
          authorized to request. The signing request using this token won't be
          able to add extra names. Use the '--principal' flag multiple times to
          configure multiple principals.

      [0;1;99m--host[0m
          Create a host certificate instead of a user certificate.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the token's validity period starts. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the token's validity period ends. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--cert-not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period ends. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h". This flag is only supported on SSH certificates.

      [0;1;99m--cert-not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period starts. If
          a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h". This flag is only supported on SSH certificates.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mname[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt or decrypt
          the private key.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          one-time token generating key.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mchain[0m
          Certificate ([0;4;39mchain[0m) in PEM format to store in the 'x5c' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'x5c' header.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-insecure[0m
          Use the JWT header 'x5cInsecure' instead of 'x5c'.

      [0;1;99m--sshpop-cert[0m=[0;4;39mchain[0m
          Certificate ([0;4;39mchain[0m) in PEM format to store in the 'sshpop' header
          of a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--sshpop-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'sshpop' header.

      [0;1;99m--nebula-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m in PEM format to store in the 'nebula' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--nebula-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'nebula' header.

      [0;1;99m--cnf[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m
          The [0;4;39mfingerprint[0m of the CSR to restrict this token for.

      [0;1;99m--cnf-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The CSR [0;4;39mfile[0m to restrict this token for.

      [0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The private key [0;4;39mfile[0m used to sign the JWT. This is usually
          downloaded from the certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--output-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The destination [0;4;39mfile[0m of the generated one-time token.

      [0;1;99m--revoke[0m
          Create a token for authorizing 'Revoke' requests. The audience will be
          invalid for any other API request.

      [0;1;99m--renew[0m
          Create a token for authorizing 'renew' requests. The audience will be
          invalid for any other API request.

      [0;1;99m--rekey[0m
          Create a token for authorizing 'rekey' requests. The audience will be
          invalid for any other API request.

      [0;1;99m--ssh[0m
          Create a token for authorizing an SSH certificate signing request.

      [0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Configure the [0;4;39mfile[0m from which to read the kubernetes service
          account token.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Most of the following examples assumes that [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m and [0;1;99m--root[0m
      are set using environment variables or the default configuration file in
      [0;4;39m$STEPPATH/config/defaults.json[0m.

      Get a new token for a DNS. Because there are no Subject Alternative Names
      configured (via the '--san' flag), the 'sans' claim of the token will have
      a default value of ['internal.example.com']:

          $ step ca token internal.example.com

      Get a new token for a 'Revoke' request:

          $ step ca token --revoke 146103349666685108195655980390445292315

      Get a new token for an IP address. Because there are no Subject
      Alternative Names configured (via the '--san' flag), the 'sans' claim of
      the token will have a default value of ['192.168.10.10']:

          $ step ca token 192.168.10.10

      Get a new token with custom Subject Alternative Names. The value of the
      'sans' claim of the token will be ['1.1.1.1', 'hello.example.com'] -
      'foobar' will not be in the 'sans' claim unless explicitly configured via
      the '--san' flag:

          $ step ca token foobar --san 1.1.1.1 --san hello.example.com

      Get a new token that expires in 30 minutes:

          $ step ca token --not-after 30m internal.example.com

      Get a new token that becomes valid in 30 minutes and expires 5 minutes
      after that:

          $ step ca token --not-before 30m --not-after 35m internal.example.com

      Get a new token with a confirmation claim to enforce a given CSR
      fingerprint:

          $ step certificate fingerprint --format base64-url-raw internal.csr
          PJLNhtQoBE1yGN_ZKzr4Y2U5pyqIGiyyszkoz2raDOw
          $ step ca token --cnf PJLNhtQoBE1yGN_ZKzr4Y2U5pyqIGiyyszkoz2raDOw internal.smallstep.com

      Get a new token with a confirmation claim to enforce the use of a given
      CSR:

          step ca token --cnf-file internal.csr internal.smallstep.com

      Get a new token signed with the given private key, the public key must be
      configured in the certificate authority:

          $ step ca token internal.smallstep.com --key token.key

      Get a new token for a specific provisioner kid, ca-url and root:

          $ step ca token internal.example.com \
              --kid 4vn46fbZT68Uxfs9LBwHkTvrjEvxQqx-W8nnE-qDjts \
              --ca-url https://ca.example.com \
              --root /path/to/root_ca.crt

      Get a new token using the simple offline mode, requires the configuration
      files, certificates, and keys created with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m:

          $ step ca token internal.example.com --offline

      Get a new token using the offline mode with all the parameters:

          $ step ca token internal.example.com \
              --offline \
              --kid 4vn46fbZT68Uxfs9LBwHkTvrjEvxQqx-W8nnE-qDjts \
              --issuer you@example.com \
              --key provisioner.key \
              --ca-url https://ca.example.com \
              --root /path/to/root_ca.crt

      Get a new token for a 'Revoke' request:

          $ step ca token --revoke 146103349666685108195655980390445292315

      Get a new token in offline mode for a 'Revoke' request:

          $ step ca token --offline --revoke 146103349666685108195655980390445292315

      Get a new token for an SSH user certificate:

          $ step ca token max@smallstep.com --ssh

      Get a new token for an SSH host certificate:

          $ step ca token my-remote.hostname --ssh --host

      Get a new token with a confirmation claim to enforce the use of a given
      public key:

          step ca token --ssh --host --cnf-file internal.pub internal.smallstep.com

      Generate a renew token and use it in a renew after expiry request:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token --x5c-cert internal.crt --x5c-key internal.key --renew internal.example.com)
          $ curl -X POST -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" https://ca.example.com/1.0/renew

      Generate a JWK provisioner token using a key in a YubiKey:

          $ step ca token --kms yubikey:pin-value=123456 --key yubikey:slot-id=82 internal.example.com

      Generate an X5C provisioner token using a certificate in a YubiKey. Note
      that a YubiKey does not support storing a certificate bundle. To make it
      work, you must add the intermediate and the root in the provisioner
      configuration:

          $ step ca token --kms yubikey:pin-value=123456 \
            --x5c-cert yubikey:slot-id=82 --x5c-key yubikey:slot-id=82 \
            internal.example.com

      Generate a token with custom data in the "user" claim. The example below
      can be accessed in a template as [0;1;99m.Token.user.field[0m, rendering to the
      string "value".

      This is distinct from [0;1;99m.Insecure.User[0m: any attributes set using this
      option are added to a claim named "user" in the signed JWT produced by this
      command. This data may therefore be considered trusted (insofar as the
      token itself is trusted).

          $ step ca token --set field=value internal.example.com

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca certificate[0m -- generate a new private key and certificate
      signed by the root certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca certificate[0m [0;4;39msubject[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
      [[0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m] [[0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--san[0m=[0;4;39mSAN[0m] [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m] [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--acme[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--standalone[0m] [[0;1;99m--webroot[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--contact[0m=[0;4;39memail[0m] [[0;1;99m--http-listen[0m=[0;4;39maddress[0m] [[0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m] [[0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m] [[0;1;99m--console[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m] [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca certificate[0m command generates a new certificate pair

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39msubject[0m
          The Common Name, DNS Name, or IP address that will be set as the
          Subject Common Name for the certificate. If no Subject Alternative
          Names (SANs) are configured (via the --san flag) then the [0;4;39msubject[0m
          will be set as the only SAN.

      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          File to write the certificate (PEM format)

      [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
          File to write the private key (PEM format)

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--san[0m=[0;4;39mdns|ip|email|uri[0m
          Add [0;4;39mdns|ip|email|uri[0m Subject Alternative Name(s) (SANs) that
          should be authorized. Use the '--san' flag multiple times to configure
          multiple SANs. The '--san' flag and the '--token' flag are mutually
          exclusive.

      [0;1;99m--attestation-ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The base url of the Attestation CA to use

      [0;1;99m--attestation-ca-root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m with trusted roots when connecting to the
          Attestation CA

      [0;1;99m--tpm-storage-directory[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The directory where TPM keys and certificates will be stored

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m
          The one-time [0;4;39mtoken[0m used to authenticate with the CA in order to
          create the certificate.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mname[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          one-time token generating key.

      [0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkty[0m
          The [0;4;39mkty[0m to build the certificate upon. If unset, default is EC.

          [0;4;39mkty[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mEC[0m
              Create an [0;1;99melliptic curve[0m keypair

            [0;1;99mOKP[0m
              Create an octet key pair (for [0;1;99m"Ed25519"[0m curve)

            [0;1;99mRSA[0m
              Create an [0;1;99mRSA[0m keypair

      [0;1;99m--crv[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m, [0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m
          The elliptic [0;4;39mcurve[0m to use for EC and OKP key types. Corresponds to
          the [0;1;99m"crv"[0m JWK parameter. Valid curves are defined in JWA [RFC7518].
          If unset, default is P-256 for EC keys and Ed25519 for OKP keys.

          [0;4;39mcurve[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mP-256[0m
              NIST P-256 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-384[0m
              NIST P-384 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-521[0m
              NIST P-521 Curve

            [0;1;99mEd25519[0m
              Ed25519 Curve

      [0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m
          The [0;4;39msize[0m (in bits) of the key for RSA and oct key types. RSA keys
          require a minimum key size of 2048 bits. If unset, default is 2048 bits
          for RSA keys and 128 bits for oct keys.

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period ends. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period starts. If
          a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--attestation-uri[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The KMS [0;4;39muri[0m used for attestation.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt or decrypt
          the private key.

      [0;1;99m--console[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining inside the terminal.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mchain[0m
          Certificate ([0;4;39mchain[0m) in PEM format to store in the 'x5c' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'x5c' header.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-chain[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m, in PEM format

      [0;1;99m--nebula-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m in PEM format to store in the 'nebula' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--nebula-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'nebula' header.

      [0;1;99m--acme[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          ACME directory [0;4;39murl[0m to be used for requesting certificates via the
          ACME protocol. Use this flag to define an ACME server other than the
          Step CA. If this flag is absent and an ACME provisioner has been
          selected then the '--ca-url' flag must be defined.

      [0;1;99m--standalone[0m
          Get a certificate using the ACME protocol and standalone mode for
          validation. Standalone is a mode in which the step process will run a
          server that will will respond to ACME challenge validation requests.
          Standalone is the default mode for serving challenge validation
          requests.

      [0;1;99m--webroot[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Specify a [0;4;39mfile[0m to use as a 'web root' for validation in the ACME
          protocol. Webroot is a mode in which the step process will write a
          challenge file to a location being served by an existing fileserver in
          order to respond to ACME challenge validation requests.

      [0;1;99m--contact[0m=[0;4;39memail-address[0m
          The [0;4;39memail-address[0m used for contact as part of the ACME protocol.
          These contacts may be used to warn of certificate expiration or other
          certificate lifetime events. Use the '--contact' flag multiple times to
          configure multiple contacts.

      [0;1;99m--http-listen[0m=[0;4;39maddress[0m
          Use a non-standard http [0;4;39maddress[0m, behind a reverse proxy or load
          balancer, for serving ACME challenges. The default address is :80,
          which requires super user (sudo) privileges. This flag must be used in
          conjunction with the '--standalone' flag.

      [0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Configure the [0;4;39mfile[0m from which to read the kubernetes service
          account token.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Request a new certificate for a given domain. There are no additional SANs
      configured, therefore (by default) the [0;4;39msubject[0m will be used as the only
      SAN extension: DNS Name internal.example.com:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token internal.example.com)
          $ step ca certificate --token $TOKEN internal.example.com internal.crt internal.key

      Request a new certificate with multiple Subject Alternative Names. The
      Subject Common Name of the certificate will be 'foobar'. However, because
      additional SANs are configured using the --san flag and 'foobar' is not one
      of these, 'foobar' will not be in the SAN extensions of the certificate.
      The certificate will have 2 IP Address extensions (1.1.1.1, 10.2.3.4) and 1
      DNS Name extension (hello.example.com):

          $ step ca certificate --san 1.1.1.1 --san hello.example.com --san 10.2.3.4 foobar internal.crt internal.key

      Request a new certificate with a 1h validity:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token internal.example.com)
          $ step ca certificate --token $TOKEN --not-after=1h internal.example.com internal.crt internal.key

      Request a new certificate using the offline mode, requires the
      configuration files, certificates, and keys created with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m:

          $ step ca certificate --offline internal.example.com internal.crt internal.key

      Request a new certificate using the offline mode with additional flags to
      avoid console prompts:

          $ step ca certificate --offline \
            --password-file ./pass.txt \
            --provisioner foo \
            --provisioner-password-file ./provisioner-pass.txt \
            internal.example.com internal.crt internal.key

      Request a new certificate using an OIDC provisioner:

          $ step ca certificate --token $(step oauth --oidc --bare) joe@example.com joe.crt joe.key

      Request a new certificate using an OIDC provisioner while remaining in the
      console:

          $ step ca certificate joe@example.com joe.crt joe.key --issuer Google --console

      Request a new certificate with an RSA public key (default is ECDSA256):

          $ step ca certificate foo.internal foo.crt foo.key --kty RSA --size 4096

      Request a new certificate with an X5C provisioner:

          $ step ca certificate foo.internal foo.crt foo.key --x5c-cert x5c.cert --x5c-key x5c.key

      [0;1;99mCertificate Templates[0m - With a provisioner configured with a custom
      template we can use the [0;1;99m--set[0m flag to pass user variables:

          $ step ca certificate foo.internal foo.crt foo.key --set emailAddresses=root@internal.com
          $ step ca certificate foo.internal foo.crt foo.key --set emailAddresses='["foo@internal.com","root@internal.com"]'

      Or you can pass them from a file using [0;1;99m--set-file[0m:

          $ cat path/to/data.json
          {
            "emailAddresses": ["foo@internal.com","root@internal.com"]
          }
          $ step ca certificate foo.internal foo.crt foo.key --set-file path/to/data.json

      [0;1;99mstep CA ACME[0m - In order to use the step CA ACME protocol you must add
      a ACME provisioner to the step CA config. See [0;1;99mstep ca provisioner add
      -h[0m.

      Request a new certificate using the step CA ACME server and a standalone
      server to serve the challenges locally (standalone mode is the default):

          $ step ca certificate foobar foo.crt foo.key --provisioner my-acme-provisioner --san foo.internal --san bar.internal

      Request a new certificate using the step CA ACME server and an existing
      server along with webroot mode to serve the challenges locally:

          $ step ca certificate foobar foo.crt foo.key --provisioner my-acme-provisioner --webroot "./acme-www" \
          --san foo.internal --san bar.internal

      Request a new certificate using the ACME protocol not served via the step
      CA (e.g. letsencrypt). NOTE: Let's Encrypt requires that the Subject Common
      Name of a requested certificate be validated as an Identifier in the ACME
      order along with any other SANS. Therefore, the Common Name must be a valid
      DNS Name. The step CA does not impose this requirement.

          $ step ca certificate foo.internal foo.crt foo.key \
          --acme https://acme-staging-v02.api.letsencrypt.org/directory --san bar.internal

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca rekey[0m -- rekey a certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca rekey[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [0;4;39mkey-file[0m [[0;1;99m--out-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--out-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--private-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m] [[0;1;99m--force[0m] [[0;1;99m--exec[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--daemon[0m] [[0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mtype[0m] [[0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m] [[0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m] [[0;1;99m--pid[0m=[0;4;39mint[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--pid-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--signal[0m=[0;4;39mint[0m] [[0;1;99m--exec[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--rekey-period[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca rekey[0m command rekeys the given certificate (with a request to
      the certificate authority) and writes the new certificate and private key
      to disk - either overwriting [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m and [0;4;39mkey-file[0m positional
      arguments or using new files when the [0;1;99m--out-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m and
      [0;1;99m--out-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m flags are used.

      With the [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag the command will periodically update the given
      certificate. By default, it will rekey the certificate before 2/3 of the
      validity period of the certificate has elapsed. A random jitter is used to
      avoid multiple instances running at the same time. The amount of time
      between rekey and certificate expiration can be configured using the
      [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m flag, or a fixed period can be set with the
      [0;1;99m--rekey-period[0m flag.

      The [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag can be combined with [0;1;99m--pid[0m, [0;1;99m--signal[0m, or
      [0;1;99m--exec[0m to provide certificate reloads on your services.

      The [0;1;99m--kms[0m flag rekeys an existing key in a KMS with another key from
      the same KMS. It does not support generating new keys, using the
      [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag, or rekeying across different KMS instances.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          The certificate in PEM format that we want to rekey.

      [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
          They key file of the certificate.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--out-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m where the new certificate will be saved to. Defaults to
          overwriting the [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m positional argument.

      [0;1;99m--out-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m to store the new private key. Defaults to overwriting the
          [0;4;39mkey-file[0m positional argument.

      [0;1;99m--private-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the private key for rekey-ing the certificate.
          By default, a new random key pair will be generated.

      [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m
          The amount of time remaining before certificate expiration, at which
          point a rekey should be attempted. The certificate rekey will not be
          performed if the time to expiration is greater than the
          [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m value. A random jitter (duration/20) will be added to
          avoid multiple services hitting the rekey endpoint at the same time.
          The [0;4;39mduration[0m is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with optional
          fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or "2h45m". Valid
          time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m", "h".

      [0;1;99m--pid[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The process id to signal after the certificate has been rekeyed. By
          default the the SIGHUP (1) signal will be used, but this can be
          configured with the [0;1;99m--signal[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--pid-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m from which to read the process id that will be signaled
          after the certificate has been rekeyed. By default the SIGHUP (1)
          signal will be used, but this can be configured with the [0;1;99m--signal[0m
          flag.

      [0;1;99m--signal[0m=[0;4;39mnumber[0m
          The signal [0;4;39mnumber[0m to send to the selected PID, so it can reload
          the configuration and load the new certificate. Default value is SIGHUP
          (1)

      [0;1;99m--exec[0m=[0;4;39mcommand[0m
          The [0;4;39mcommand[0m to run after the certificate has been rekeyed.

      [0;1;99m--daemon[0m
          Run the rekey command as a daemon, rekeying and overwriting the
          certificate periodically. By default the daemon will rekey a
          certificate before 2/3 of the time to expiration has elapsed. The
          period can be configured using the [0;1;99m--rekey-period[0m or
          [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m flags.

      [0;1;99m--rekey-period[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m
          The period with which to schedule rekeying of the certificate in
          daemon mode. Requires the [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag. The [0;4;39mduration[0m is a
          sequence of decimal numbers, each with optional fraction and a unit
          suffix, such as "300ms", "1.5h", or "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns",
          "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m", "h".

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkty[0m
          The [0;4;39mkty[0m to build the certificate upon. If unset, default is EC.

          [0;4;39mkty[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mEC[0m
              Create an [0;1;99melliptic curve[0m keypair

            [0;1;99mOKP[0m
              Create an octet key pair (for [0;1;99m"Ed25519"[0m curve)

            [0;1;99mRSA[0m
              Create an [0;1;99mRSA[0m keypair

      [0;1;99m--crv[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m, [0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m
          The elliptic [0;4;39mcurve[0m to use for EC and OKP key types. Corresponds to
          the [0;1;99m"crv"[0m JWK parameter. Valid curves are defined in JWA [RFC7518].
          If unset, default is P-256 for EC keys and Ed25519 for OKP keys.

          [0;4;39mcurve[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mP-256[0m
              NIST P-256 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-384[0m
              NIST P-384 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-521[0m
              NIST P-521 Curve

            [0;1;99mEd25519[0m
              Ed25519 Curve

      [0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m
          The [0;4;39msize[0m (in bits) of the key for RSA and oct key types. RSA keys
          require a minimum key size of 2048 bits. If unset, default is 2048 bits
          for RSA keys and 128 bits for oct keys.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt or decrypt
          the private key.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Rekey a certificate:

          $ step ca rekey internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey a certificate without overwriting the existing certificate and key:

          $ step ca rekey --out-cert out.crt --out-key out.key internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey a certificate forcing the overwrite of the previous certificate and
      key (overwrites the existing files without prompting):

          $ step ca rekey --force internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey a certificate which key is in a KMS, with another from the same KMS:

          $ step ca rekey \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            --private-key 'pkcs11:id=4002'
            pkcs11.crt 'pkcs11:id=4001'

      Rekey a certificate providing the [0;4;39m--ca-url[0m and [0;4;39m--root[0m flags:

          $ step ca rekey --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com:9000 \
            --root /path/to/root_ca.crt internal.crt internal.key
          Would you like to overwrite internal.crt [Y/n]: y

      Rekey a certificate only if it expires within the given time frame:

          $ step ca rekey --expires-in 8h internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey the certificate before 2/3 of the validity has passed:

          $ step ca rekey --daemon internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey the certificate before 8 hours and 30m of the expiration time:

          $ step ca rekey --daemon --expires-in 8h30m internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey the certificate every 16h:

          $ step ca rekey --daemon --rekey-period 16h internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey the certificate and reload nginx:

          $ step ca rekey --daemon --exec "nginx -s reload" internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey the certificate and convert it to DER:

          $ step ca rekey --daemon --rekey-period 16h \
            --exec "step certificate format --force --out internal.der internal.crt" \
            internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey a certificate using the offline mode, requires the configuration
      files, certificates, and keys created with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m:

          $ step ca rekey --offline internal.crt internal.key

      Rekey the certificate and write it to specified files:

          $ step ca rekey internal.crt internal.key --out-crt foo.crt --out-key foo.key

      Rekey the certificate using a given private key:

          $ step ca rekey internal.crt internal.key --private-key foo.key

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca renew[0m -- renew a certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca renew[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [0;4;39mkey-file[0m [[0;1;99m--mtls[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m] [[0;1;99m--force[0m] [[0;1;99m--pid[0m=[0;4;39mint[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--pid-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--signal[0m=[0;4;39mint[0m] [[0;1;99m--exec[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--daemon[0m] [[0;1;99m--renew-period[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m] [[0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca renew[0m command renews the given certificate (with a request to
      the certificate authority) and writes the new certificate to disk - either
      overwriting [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m or using a new file when the [0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
      flag is used.

      With the [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag the command will periodically update the given
      certificate. By default, it will renew the certificate before 2/3 of the
      validity period of the certificate has elapsed. A random jitter is used to
      avoid multiple instances running at the same time. The amount of time
      between renewal and certificate expiration can be configured using the
      [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m flag, or a fixed period can be set with the
      [0;1;99m--renew-period[0m flag.

      The [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag can be combined with [0;1;99m--pid[0m, [0;1;99m--signal[0m, or
      [0;1;99m--exec[0m to provide certificate reloads on your services.

      By default, the renew command authenticates to step-ca using mTLS, except
      when the certificate is expired and renewal after expiry is allowed by the
      CA.

      There are scenarios where mTLS is not possible: When step-ca is behind a
      layer 7 proxy, when the server's leaf certificate EKU is not configured for
      client authentication, or when the server is a StepCAS RA for an upstream
      step-ca server. For these scenarios, use [0;1;99m--mtls=false[0m to force a flow
      that uses X5C token-based authentication.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          The certificate in PEM format that we want to renew.

      [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
          They key file of the certificate.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--mtls[0m
          Use mTLS to renew a certificate. Use --mtls=false to force the token
          authorization flow instead.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt or decrypt
          the private key.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--out[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m, [0;1;99m--output-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The new certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m path. Defaults to overwriting the
          [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m positional argument

      [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m
          The amount of time remaining before certificate expiration, at which
          point a renewal should be attempted. The certificate renewal will not
          be performed if the time to expiration is greater than the
          [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m value. A random jitter (duration/20) will be added to
          avoid multiple services hitting the renew endpoint at the same time.
          The [0;4;39mduration[0m is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with optional
          fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or "2h45m". Valid
          time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m", "h".

      [0;1;99m--pid[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The process id to signal after the certificate has been renewed. By
          default the the SIGHUP (1) signal will be used, but this can be
          configured with the [0;1;99m--signal[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--pid-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m from which to read the process id that will be signaled
          after the certificate has been renewed. By default the SIGHUP (1)
          signal will be used, but this can be configured with the [0;1;99m--signal[0m
          flag.

      [0;1;99m--signal[0m=[0;4;39mnumber[0m
