          The signal [0;4;39mnumber[0m to send to the selected PID, so it can reload
          the configuration and load the new certificate. Default value is SIGHUP
          (1)

      [0;1;99m--exec[0m=[0;4;39mcommand[0m
          The [0;4;39mcommand[0m to run after the certificate has been renewed.

      [0;1;99m--daemon[0m
          Run the renew command as a daemon, renewing and overwriting the
          certificate periodically. By default the daemon will renew a
          certificate before 2/3 of the time to expiration has elapsed. The
          period can be configured using the [0;1;99m--renew-period[0m or
          [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m flags.

      [0;1;99m--renew-period[0m=[0;4;39mduration[0m
          The period with which to schedule renewals of the certificate in
          daemon mode. Requires the [0;1;99m--daemon[0m flag. The [0;4;39mduration[0m is a
          sequence of decimal numbers, each with optional fraction and a unit
          suffix, such as "300ms", "1.5h", or "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns",
          "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m", "h".

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Renew a certificate with the configured CA:

          $ step ca renew internal.crt internal.key
          Would you like to overwrite internal.crt [Y/n]: y

      Renew a certificate without overwriting the previous certificate:

          $ step ca renew --out renewed.crt internal.crt internal.key

      Renew a certificate forcing the overwrite of the previous certificate:

          $ step ca renew --force internal.crt internal.key

      Renew a certificate using the token flow instead of mTLS:

          $ step ca renew --mtls=false --force internal.crt internal.key

      Renew a certificate which key is in a KMS:

          $ step ca renew \
            --kms 'pkcs11:module-path=/usr/local/lib/softhsm/libsofthsm2.so;token=smallstep?pin-value=password' \
            pkcs11.crt 'pkcs11:id=4001'

      Renew a certificate providing the [0;4;39m--ca-url[0m and [0;4;39m--root[0m flags:

          $ step ca renew --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com:9000 \
            --root /path/to/root_ca.crt internal.crt internal.key
          Would you like to overwrite internal.crt [Y/n]: y

      Renew skipped because it was too early:

          $ step ca renew --expires-in 8h internal.crt internal.key
          certificate not renewed: expires in 10h52m5s

      Renew the certificate before 2/3 of the validity has passed:

          $ step ca renew --daemon internal.crt internal.key

      Renew the certificate before 8 hours and 30m of the expiration time:

          $ step ca renew --daemon --expires-in 8h30m internal.crt internal.key

      Renew the certificate every 16h:

          $ step ca renew --daemon --renew-period 16h internal.crt internal.key

      Renew the certificate and reload nginx:

          $ step ca renew --daemon --exec "nginx -s reload" internal.crt internal.key

      Renew the certificate and convert it to DER:

          $ step ca renew --daemon --renew-period 16h \
            --exec "step certificate format --force --out internal.der internal.crt" \
            internal.crt internal.key

      Renew a certificate using the offline mode, requires the configuration
      files, certificates, and keys created with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m:

          $ step ca renew --offline internal.crt internal.key

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca revoke[0m -- revoke a certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca revoke[0m [0;4;39mserial-number[0m [[0;1;99m--cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mott[0m] [[0;1;99m--reason[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--reasonCode[0m=[0;4;39mcode[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca revoke[0m command revokes a certificate with the given serial
      number.

      [0;1;99mActive Revocation[0m: A certificate is no longer valid from the moment it
      has been actively revoked. Clients are required to check against
      centralized sources of certificate validity information (e.g. by using CRLs
      (Certificate Revocation Lists) or OCSP (Online Certificate Status
      Protocol)) to verify that certificates have not been revoked. Active
      Revocation requires clients to take an active role in certificate
      validation for the benefit of real time revocation.

      [0;1;99mPassive Revocation[0m: A certificate that has been passively revoked can
      no longer be renewed. It will still be valid for the remainder of it's
      validity period, but cannot be prolonged. The benefit of passive revocation
      is that clients can verify certificates in a simple, decentralized manner
      without relying on centralized 3rd parties. Passive revocation works best
      with short certificate lifetimes.

      A revocation request can be authorized using a JWK provisioner token, or
      using a client certificate.

      When you supply a serial number, you're prompted to choose a provisioner,
      and a provisioner token is transparently generated. Any JWK provisioner can
      revoke any certificate.

      When you supply a certificate and private key (with --crt and --key), mTLS
      is used to authorize the revocation.

      Certificates generated using an OIDC provisioner cannot be revoked by
      their serial number.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mserial-number[0m
          The serial number of the certificate that should be revoked. Can be
          left blank, either to be supplied by prompt, or when using the --cert
          and --key flags for revocation over mTLS.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the cert that should be revoked.

      [0;1;99m--key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the key corresponding to the cert that should
          be revoked.

      [0;1;99m--reason[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m
          The [0;4;39mstring[0m representing the reason for which the cert is being
          revoked.

      [0;1;99m--reasonCode[0m=[0;4;39mreasonCode[0m
          The [0;4;39mreasonCode[0m specifies the reason for revocation - chose from a
          list of common revocation reasons. If unset, the default is
          Unspecified.

          [0;4;39mreasonCode[0m can be a number from 0-9 or a case insensitive string
          matching one of the following options:

            [0;1;99mUnspecified[0m
              No reason given (Default -- reasonCode=0).

            [0;1;99mKeyCompromise[0m
              The key is believed to have been compromised (reasonCode=1).

            [0;1;99mCACompromise[0m
              The issuing Certificate Authority itself has been compromised (reasonCode=2).

            [0;1;99mAffiliationChanged[0m
              The certificate contained affiliation information, for example, it may
              have been an EV certificate and the associated business is no longer owned by
              the same entity (reasonCode=3).

            [0;1;99mSuperseded[0m
              The certificate is being replaced (reasonCode=4).

            [0;1;99mCessationOfOperation[0m
              If a CA is decommissioned, no longer to be used, the CA's certificate
              should be revoked with this reason code. Do not revoke the CA's certificate if
              the CA no longer issues new certificates, yet still publishes CRLs for the
              currently issued certificates (reasonCode=5).

            [0;1;99mCertificateHold[0m
              A temporary revocation that indicates that a CA will not vouch for a
              certificate at a specific point in time. Once a certificate is revoked with a
              CertificateHold reason code, the certificate can then be revoked with another
              Reason Code, or unrevoked and returned to use (reasonCode=6).

            [0;1;99mRemoveFromCRL[0m
              If a certificate is revoked with the CertificateHold reason code, it is
              possible to "unrevoke" a certificate. The unrevoking process still lists the
              certificate in the CRL, but with the reason code set to RemoveFromCRL.
              Note: This is specific to the CertificateHold reason and is only used in DeltaCRLs
              (reasonCode=8).

            [0;1;99mPrivilegeWithdrawn[0m
              The right to represent the given entity was revoked for some reason
              (reasonCode=9).

            [0;1;99mAACompromise[0m
              It is known or suspected that aspects of the AA validated in the
              attribute certificate have been compromised (reasonCode=10).

      [0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m
          The one-time [0;4;39mtoken[0m used to authenticate with the CA in order to
          create the certificate.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Revoke a certificate using a transparently generated JWK provisioner token
      and the default 'unspecified' reason:

          $ step ca revoke 308893286343609293989051180431574390766

      Revoke a certificate using a transparently generated token and configured
      reason and reasonCode:

          $ step ca revoke --reason "laptop compromised" --reasonCode 1 308893286343609293989051180431574390766

      Revoke a certificate using a transparently generated token and configured
      reason and stringified reasonCode:

          $ step ca revoke --reason "laptop compromised" --reasonCode "key compromise" 308893286343609293989051180431574390766

      Revoke a certificate using that same certificate to validate and authorize
      the request (rather than a token) over mTLS:

          $ step ca revoke --cert mike.cert --key mike.key

      Revoke a certificate using a JWK token, pre-generated by a provisioner, to
      authorize the request with the CA:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token --revoke 308893286343609293989051180431574390766)
          $ step ca revoke --token $TOKEN 308893286343609293989051180431574390766

      Revoke a certificate in offline mode:

          $ step ca revoke --offline 308893286343609293989051180431574390766

      Revoke a certificate in offline mode using --cert and --key (the cert/key
      pair will be validated against the root and intermediate certificates
      configured in the step CA):

          $ step ca revoke --offline --cert foo.crt --key foo.key

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca provisioner[0m -- create and manage the certificate authority
      provisioners

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca provisioner[0m [0;4;39mcommand[0m [0;4;39m[options][0m [0;4;39m[arguments][0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca provisioner[0m command group provides facilities for managing the
      certificate authority provisioners.

      A provisioner is an entity that controls provisioning credentials, which
      are used to generate provisioning tokens.

      Provisioning credentials are simple JWK key pairs using public-key
      cryptography. The public key is used to verify a provisioning token while
      the private key is used to sign the provisioning token.

      Provisioning tokens are JWT tokens signed by the JWK private key. These
      JWT tokens are used to get a valid TLS certificate from the certificate
      authority. Each provisioner is able to manage a different set of rules that
      can be used to configure the bounds of the certificate.

      In the certificate authority, a provisioner is configured with a JSON
      object with the following properties:

          • [0;1;99mname[0m: the provisioner name, it will become the JWT issuer and a
          good practice is to use an email address for this.

          • [0;1;99mtype[0m: the provisioner type, currently only "jwk" is supported.

          • [0;1;99mkey[0m: the JWK public key used to verify the provisioning tokens.

          • [0;1;99mencryptedKey[0m (optional): the JWE compact serialization of the
          private key used to sign the provisioning tokens.

          • [0;1;99mclaims[0m (optional): an object with custom options for each
          provisioner. Options supported are:

              • [0;1;99mminTLSCertDuration[0m: minimum duration of a certificate, set to
              5m by default.

              • [0;1;99mmaxTLSCertDuration[0m: maximum duration of a certificate, set to
              24h by default.

              • [0;1;99mdefaultTLSCertDuration[0m: default duration of the certificate,
              set to 24h by default.

              • [0;1;99mdisableRenewal[0m: whether or not to disable certificate renewal,
              set to false by default.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--help[0m, [0;1;99m-h[0m
          show help

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      List the active provisioners:

          $ step ca provisioner list

      Retrieve the encrypted private jwk for the given kid:

          $ step ca provisioner jwe-key 1234 --ca-url https://127.0.0.1 --root ./root.crt

      Add a single provisioner:

          $ step ca provisioner add max@smallstep.com max-laptop.jwk --ca-config ca.json

      Remove the provisioner matching a given issuer and kid:

          $ step ca provisioner remove max@smallstep.com --kid 1234 --ca-config ca.json

[0;1;99mCOMMANDS[0m
      [0;1;99mlist[0m     list provisioners configured in the CA           
      [0;1;99mjwe-key[0m  retrieve and print a provisioning key in the CA  
      [0;1;99madd[0m      add a provisioner                                
      [0;1;99mupdate[0m   update a provisioner                             
      [0;1;99mremove[0m   remove a provisioner from the CA configuration   
      [0;1;99mwebhook[0m  create and manage webhooks for a provisioner     

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca sign[0m -- generate a new certificate from signing a certificate
      request

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca sign[0m [0;4;39mcsr-file[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m [[0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0m--set[0;1;99m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m] [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--acme[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0m--standalone[0;1;99m] [[0;1;99m--webroot[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--contact[0m=[0;4;39memail[0m]
      [[0m--http-listen[0;1;99m=[0;4;39maddress[0m] [[0;1;99m--console[0m] [[0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0m--x5c-key[0;1;99m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m]
      [[0m--password-file[0;1;99m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0m--context**=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca sign[0m command signs the given csr and generates a new
      certificate.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcsr-file[0m
          File with the certificate signing request (PEM format)

      [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
          File to write the certificate (PEM format)

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m
          The one-time [0;4;39mtoken[0m used to authenticate with the CA in order to
          create the certificate.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mname[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          one-time token generating key.

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period starts. If
          a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period ends. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt or decrypt
          the private key.

      [0;1;99m--console[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining inside the terminal.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mchain[0m
          Certificate ([0;4;39mchain[0m) in PEM format to store in the 'x5c' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'x5c' header.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-chain[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m, in PEM format

      [0;1;99m--nebula-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m in PEM format to store in the 'nebula' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--nebula-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'nebula' header.

      [0;1;99m--acme[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          ACME directory [0;4;39murl[0m to be used for requesting certificates via the
          ACME protocol. Use this flag to define an ACME server other than the
          Step CA. If this flag is absent and an ACME provisioner has been
          selected then the '--ca-url' flag must be defined.

      [0;1;99m--standalone[0m
          Get a certificate using the ACME protocol and standalone mode for
          validation. Standalone is a mode in which the step process will run a
          server that will will respond to ACME challenge validation requests.
          Standalone is the default mode for serving challenge validation
          requests.

      [0;1;99m--webroot[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Specify a [0;4;39mfile[0m to use as a 'web root' for validation in the ACME
          protocol. Webroot is a mode in which the step process will write a
          challenge file to a location being served by an existing fileserver in
          order to respond to ACME challenge validation requests.

      [0;1;99m--contact[0m=[0;4;39memail-address[0m
          The [0;4;39memail-address[0m used for contact as part of the ACME protocol.
          These contacts may be used to warn of certificate expiration or other
          certificate lifetime events. Use the '--contact' flag multiple times to
          configure multiple contacts.

      [0;1;99m--http-listen[0m=[0;4;39maddress[0m
          Use a non-standard http [0;4;39maddress[0m, behind a reverse proxy or load
          balancer, for serving ACME challenges. The default address is :80,
          which requires super user (sudo) privileges. This flag must be used in
          conjunction with the '--standalone' flag.

      [0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Configure the [0;4;39mfile[0m from which to read the kubernetes service
          account token.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Sign a new certificate for the given CSR:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token internal.example.com)
          $ step ca sign --token $TOKEN internal.csr internal.crt

      Sign a new certificate with a 1h validity:

          $ TOKEN=$(step ca token internal.example.com)
          $ step ca sign --token $TOKEN --not-after=1h internal.csr internal.crt

      Sign a new certificate using the offline mode, requires the configuration
      files, certificates, and keys created with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m:

          $ step ca sign --offline internal internal.csr internal.crt

      Sign a new certificate using the offline mode with additional flag to
      avoid console prompts:

          $ step ca sign --offline --password-file ./pass.txt internal internal.csr internal.crt

      Sign a new certificate using an X5C provisioner: NOTE: You must have a X5C
      provisioner configured (using [0;1;99mstep ca provisioner add[0m).

          $ step ca sign foo.internal foo.csr foo.crt --x5c-cert leaf-x5c.crt --x5c-key leaf-x5c.key

      [0;1;99mCertificate Templates[0m - With a provisioner configured with a custom
      template we can use the [0;1;99m--set[0m flag to pass user variables:

          $ step ca sign foo.csr foo.crt --set dnsNames=foo.internal.com
          $ step ca sign foo.csr foo.crt --set dnsNames='["foo.internal.com","bar.internal.com"]'

      Or you can pass them from a file using [0;1;99m--set-file[0m:

          $ cat path/to/data.json
          {
            "dnsNames": ["foo.internal.com","bar.internal.com"]
          }
          $ step ca sign foo.csr foo.crt --set-file path/to/data.json

      [0;1;99mstep CA ACME[0m - In order to use the step CA ACME protocol you must add
      a ACME provisioner to the step CA config. See [0;1;99mstep ca provisioner add
      -h[0m.

      Sign a CSR using the step CA ACME server and a standalone server to serve
      the challenges locally (standalone mode is the default):

          $ step ca sign foo.csr foo.crt --provisioner my-acme-provisioner

      Sign a CSR using the step CA ACME server and an existing server along with
      webroot mode to serve the challenges locally:

          $ step ca sign foo.csr foo.crt \
            --provisioner my-acme-provisioner --webroot "./acme-www" \

      Sign a CSR using the ACME protocol served by another online CA (not step
      CA, e.g. letsencrypt). NOTE: Let's Encrypt requires that the Subject Common
      Name of a requested certificate be validated as an Identifier in the ACME
      order along with any other SANS. Therefore, the Common Name must be a valid
      DNS Name. The step CA does not impose this requirement.

          $ step ca sign foo.csr foo.crt \
          --acme https://acme-staging-v02.api.letsencrypt.org/directory

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca root[0m -- download and validate the root certificate

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca root[0m [[0;4;39mroot-file[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--fingerprint[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca root[0m downloads and validates the root certificate from the
      certificate authority.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mroot-file[0m
          File to write root certificate (PEM format)

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--fingerprint[0m=[0;4;39mfingerprint[0m
          The [0;4;39mfingerprint[0m of the targeted root certificate.

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Get the root fingerprint in the CA:

          $ step certificate fingerprint /path/to/root_ca.crt
          0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3

      Download the root certificate from the configured certificate authority:

          $ step ca root root_ca.crt \
            --fingerprint 0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3

      Download the root certificate using a given certificate authority:

          $ step ca root root_ca.crt \
            --ca-url https://ca.smallstep.com:9000 \
            --fingerprint 0d7d3834cf187726cf331c40a31aa7ef6b29ba4df601416c9788f6ee01058cf3

      Print the root certificate using the flags set by [0;4;39mstep ca bootstrap[0m:

          $ step ca root

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca roots[0m -- download all the root certificates

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca roots[0m [[0;4;39mroots-file[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m

      certificates.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m

          File to write all the root certificates (PEM format)

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m

      Download the roots with custom flags:

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca admin[0m -- create and manage the certificate authority admins

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca admin[0m [0;4;39mcommand[0m [0;4;39m[options][0m [0;4;39m[arguments][0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ca admin[0m command group provides facilities for managing the
      certificate authority admins.

      An admin is an entity that manages administrative resources (like
      authority configuration, provisioner configuration, and other admins)
      within a certificate authority.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--help[0m, [0;1;99m-h[0m
          show help

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      List the active admins:

          $ step ca admin list

      Add an admin:

          $ step ca admin add max@smallstep.com my-jwk-provisioner --super

      Update an admin:

          $ step ca admin update max@smallstep.com --super=false

      Remove an admin:

          $ step ca admin remove max@smallstep.com

[0;1;99mCOMMANDS[0m
      [0;1;99mlist[0m    list all admins in the CA configuration    
      [0;1;99madd[0m     add an admin to the CA configuration       
      [0;1;99mremove[0m  remove an admin from the CA configuration  
      [0;1;99mupdate[0m  update an admin                            

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh[0m -- create and manage ssh certificates

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh[0m [0;4;39mcommand[0m [0;4;39m[options][0m [0;4;39m[arguments][0m

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh[0m command group provides facilities to sign SSH certificates.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--help[0m, [0;1;99m-h[0m
          show help

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Generate a new SSH key pair and user certificate:

          $ step ssh certificate joe@work id_ecdsa

      Generate a new SSH key pair and host certificate:

          $ step ssh certificate --host internal.example.com ssh_host_ecdsa_key

      Add a new user certificate to the agent:

          $ step ssh login joe@example.com

      Remove a certificate from the agent:

          $ step ssh logout joe@example.com

      List all keys in the agent:

          $ step ssh list

      Configure a user environment with the SSH templates:

          $ step ssh config

      Inspect an ssh certificate file:

          $ step ssh inspect id_ecdsa-cert.pub

      Inspect an ssh certificate in the agent:

          $ step ssh list --raw joe@example.com | step ssh inspect

      List all the hosts you have access to:

          $ step ssh hosts

      Login into one host:

          $ ssh internal.example.com

[0;1;99mCOMMANDS[0m
      [0;1;99mcertificate[0m    sign a SSH certificate using the SSH CA                    
      [0;1;99mcheck-host[0m     checks if a certificate has been issued for a host         
      [0;1;99mconfig[0m         configures ssh to be used with certificates                
      [0;1;99mfingerprint[0m    print the fingerprint of an SSH public key or certificate  
      [0;1;99mhosts[0m          returns a list of all valid hosts                          
      [0;1;99minspect[0m        print the contents of an ssh certificate                   
      [0;1;99mlist[0m           list public keys known to the ssh agent                    
      [0;1;99mlogin[0m          adds a SSH certificate into the authentication agent       
      [0;1;99mlogout[0m         removes a private key from the ssh-agent                   
      [0;1;99mneeds-renewal[0m  Check if an SSH certificate needs to be renewed            
      [0;1;99mproxycommand[0m   proxy ssh connections according to the host registry       
      [0;1;99mrekey[0m          rekey a SSH certificate using the SSH CA                   
      [0;1;99mrenew[0m          renew a SSH certificate using the SSH CA                   
      [0;1;99mrevoke[0m         revoke a SSH certificate using the SSH CA                  

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh certificate[0m -- sign a SSH certificate using the SSH CA

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh certificate[0m [0;4;39mkey-id[0m [0;4;39mkey-file[0m [[0;1;99m--host[0m]
      [--[0;1;99mhost-id[0m] [[0;1;99m--sign[0m] [[0;1;99m--principal[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--add-user[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--comment[0m=[0;4;39mcomment[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m] [[0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--console[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--no-password[0m] [[0;1;99m--insecure[0m] [[0;1;99m--force[0m] [[0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--no-agent[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkey-type[0m] [[0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m] [[0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--min-password-length[0m=[0;4;39mlength[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh certificate[0m command generates an SSH key pair and creates a
      certificate using [0;1;39mstep certificates[0m.

      With a certificate clients or servers may trust only the CA key and verify
      its signature on a certificate rather than trusting many user/host keys.

      Note that not all the provisioner types will be able to generate user and
      host certificates. Currently JWK provisioners can generate both, but with
      an OIDC provisioner you will only be able to generate user certificates
      unless you are and admin that can generate both. With a cloud identity
      provisioner you will only be able to generate host certificates.

      To configure a server to accept user certificates and provide a user
      certificate you need to add the following lines in
      [0;4;39m/etc/ssh/sshd_config[0m:

          # The path to the CA public key, it accepts multiple user CAs, one per line
          TrustedUserCAKeys /etc/ssh/ssh_user_key.pub
          
          # Path to the private key and certificate
          HostKey /etc/ssh/ssh_host_ecdsa_key
          HostCertificate /etc/ssh/ssh_host_ecdsa_key-cert.pub

      Make sure to restart the sshd daemon to refresh its configuration.

      To configure clients to accept host certificates you need to add the host
      CA public key in [0;4;39m~/.ssh/known_hosts[0m with the following format:

          @cert-authority *example.com ecdsa-sha2-nistp256 AAAAE...=

      Where [0;4;39m*.example.com[0m is a pattern that matches the hosts and
      [0;4;39mecdsa-sha2-nistp256 AAAAE...=[0m should be the contents of the host CA
      public key.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mkey-id[0m
          The certificate identity. If no principals are passed we will use the
          key-id as a principal, if it has the format abc@def then the principal
          will be abc.

      [0;4;39mkey-file[0m
          The private key name when generating a new key pair, or the public key
          path when we are just signing it.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m

      [0;1;99m--no-password[0m
          Do not ask for a password to encrypt a private key. Sensitive key
          material will be written to disk unencrypted. This is not recommended.
          Requires [0;1;99m--insecure[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period starts. If
          a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period ends. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mname[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m
          The one-time [0;4;39mtoken[0m used to authenticate with the CA in order to
          create the certificate.

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--console[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining inside the terminal.

      [0;1;99m--add-user[0m
          Create a user provisioner certificate used to create a new user.

      [0;1;99m--host[0m
          Create a host certificate instead of a user certificate.

      [0;1;99m--host-id[0m=[0;4;39mUUID[0m
          Specify a [0;4;39mUUID[0m to identify the host rather than using an
          auto-generated UUID. If "machine" is passed, derive a UUID from
          "/etc/machine-id."

      [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to encrypt the
          private key.

      [0;1;99m--principal[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m-n[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          Add the specified principal (user or host [0;4;39mname[0ms) to the
          certificate request. This flag can be used multiple times. However, it
          cannot be used in conjunction with '--token' when requesting
          certificates from OIDC, JWK, and X5C provisioners, or from any
          provisioner with 'disableCustomSANs' set to 'true'. These provisioners
          will use the contents of the token to determine the principals.

      [0;1;99m--private-key[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          When signing an existing public key, use this flag to specify the
          corresponding private key so that the pair can be added to an SSH
          Agent.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          one-time token generating key.

      [0;1;99m--sign[0m
          Sign the public key passed as an argument instead of creating one.

      [0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkty[0m
          The [0;4;39mkty[0m to build the certificate upon. If unset, default is EC.

          [0;4;39mkty[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mEC[0m
              Create an [0;1;99melliptic curve[0m keypair

            [0;1;99mOKP[0m
              Create an octet key pair (for [0;1;99m"Ed25519"[0m curve)

            [0;1;99mRSA[0m
              Create an [0;1;99mRSA[0m keypair

      [0;1;99m--crv[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m, [0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m
          The elliptic [0;4;39mcurve[0m to use for EC and OKP key types. Corresponds to
          the [0;1;99m"crv"[0m JWK parameter. Valid curves are defined in JWA [RFC7518].
          If unset, default is P-256 for EC keys and Ed25519 for OKP keys.

          [0;4;39mcurve[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mP-256[0m
              NIST P-256 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-384[0m
              NIST P-384 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-521[0m
              NIST P-521 Curve

            [0;1;99mEd25519[0m
              Ed25519 Curve

      [0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m
          The [0;4;39msize[0m (in bits) of the key for RSA and oct key types. RSA keys
          require a minimum key size of 2048 bits. If unset, default is 2048 bits
          for RSA keys and 128 bits for oct keys.

      [0;1;99m--comment[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The comment used when adding the certificate to an agent. Defaults to
          the subject if not provided.

      [0;1;99m--kms[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m
          The [0;4;39muri[0m to configure a Cloud KMS or an HSM.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-cert[0m=[0;4;39mchain[0m
          Certificate ([0;4;39mchain[0m) in PEM format to store in the 'x5c' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'x5c' header.

      [0;1;99m--x5c-chain[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m, in PEM format

      [0;1;99m--nebula-cert[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Certificate [0;4;39mfile[0m in PEM format to store in the 'nebula' header of
          a JWT.

      [0;1;99m--nebula-key[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Private key [0;4;39mfile[0m, used to sign a JWT, corresponding to the
          certificate that will be stored in the 'nebula' header.

      [0;1;99m--k8ssa-token-path[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          Configure the [0;4;39mfile[0m from which to read the kubernetes service
          account token.

      [0;1;99m--no-agent[0m
          Do not add the generated certificate and associated private key to the
          SSH agent.

      [0;1;99m--min-password-length[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Set minimum required length for password used to encrypt private key.
          The default value is '0'. Values `=0 are interpreted as if no minimum
          value is set.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Generate a new SSH key pair and user certificate:

          $ step ssh certificate mariano@work id_ecdsa

      Generate a new SSH key pair and user certificate and do not add to SSH
      agent:

          $ step ssh certificate mariano@work id_ecdsa --no-agent

      Generate a new SSH key pair and user certificate and set the lifetime to
      2hrs:

          $ step ssh certificate mariano@work id_ecdsa --not-after 2h

      Generate a new SSH key pair and user certificate and set the lifetime to
      begin 2hrs from now and last for 8hrs:

          $ step ssh certificate mariano@work id_ecdsa --not-before 2h --not-after 10h

      Sign an SSH public key and generate a user certificate:

          $ step ssh certificate --sign mariano@work id_ecdsa.pub

      Generate a new SSH key pair and host certificate:

          $ step ssh certificate --host internal.example.com ssh_host_ecdsa_key

      Sign an SSH public key and generate a host certificate:

          $ step ssh certificate --host --sign \
            internal.example.com ssh_host_ecdsa_key.pub

      Sign an SSH public key and generate a host certificate with a custom uuid:

          $ step ssh certificate --host --host-id 00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000 \
            --sign internal.example.com ssh_host_ecdsa_key.pub

      Sign an SSH public key and generate a host certificate with a uuid derived
      from '/etc/machine-id':

          $ step ssh certificate --host --host-id machine --sign \
            internal.example.com ssh_host_ecdsa_key.pub

      Generate an ssh certificate with custom principals from an existing key
      pair and add the certificate to the ssh agent:

          $ step ssh certificate --principal max --principal mariano --sign \
            ops@work id_ecdsa.pub --private-key id_ecdsa_key

      Generate a new key pair and a certificate using a given token:

          $ step ssh certificate --token $TOKEN mariano@work id_ecdsa

      Create an EC pair with curve P-521 and certificate:

          $  step ssh certificate --kty EC --curve "P-521" mariano@work id_ecdsa

      Create an Octet Key Pair with curve Ed25519 and certificate:

          $  step ssh certificate --kty OKP --curve Ed25519 mariano@work id_ed25519

[0;1;99mNAME[0m

      [[0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh check-host[0m checks if a certificate has been issued for a
      host.

      This command returns a zero exit status if the host has a certificate.
      Otherwise, it returns 1.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mhostname[0m
          The hostname of the server to check.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--verbose[0m, [0;1;99m-v[0m
          Return "true" or "false" in the terminal.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Check that internal.example.com exists:

          $ step ssh check-host internal.smallstep.com

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh config[0m -- configures ssh to be used with certificates

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh config[0m [[0;1;99m--team[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--team-authority[0m=[0;4;39msub-domain[0m] [[0;1;99m--host[0m] [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--dry-run[0m] [[0;1;99m--roots[0m] [[0;1;99m--federation[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--console[0m] [[0;1;99m--force[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh config[0m configures SSH to be used with certificates. It also
      supports flags to inspect the root certificates used to sign the
      certificates.

      This command uses the templates defined in step-certificates to set up
      user and hosts environments.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--host[0m
          Configures a SSH server instead of a client.

      [0;1;99m--team[0m=[0;4;39mID[0m
          The team [0;4;39mID[0m used to bootstrap the environment.

      [0;1;99m--team-authority[0m=[0;4;39msub-domain[0m
          The [0;4;39msub-domain[0m of the certificate authority to bootstrap. E.g.,
          for an authority with domain name 'certs.example-team.ca.smallstep.com'
          the value would be 'certs'.

      [0;1;99m--team-url[0m=[0;4;39murl[0m
          The [0;4;39murl[0m step queries to retrieve initial team configuration. Only
          used with the [0;1;99m--team[0m option. If the url contains [0;4;39m<>[0m
          placeholders, they are replaced with the team ID. Replacing the
          authority-id section of the url is not supported with placeholders.

      [0;1;99m--roots[0m
          Prints the public keys used to verify user or host certificates.

      [0;1;99m--federation[0m
          Prints all the public keys in the federation. These keys are used to
          verify user or host certificates

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m used as a variable in the templates. Use the flag
          multiple times to set multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--console[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining inside the terminal.

      [0;1;99m--dry-run[0m
          Executes the command without changing any file.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m of the context for the new authority.

      [0;1;99m--profile[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m that will serve as the profile name for the context.

      [0;1;99m--authority[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The [0;4;39mname[0m that will serve as the authority name for the context.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Print the public keys used to verify user certificates:

          $ step ssh config --roots

      Print the public keys used to verify host certificates:

          $ step ssh config --host --roots

      Apply configuration templates on the user system:

          $ step ssh config

      Apply configuration templates on a host:

          $ step ssh config --host

      Apply configuration templates with custom variables:

          $ step ssh config --set User=joe --set Bastion=bastion.example.com

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh list[0m -- list public keys known to the ssh agent

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh list[0m [[0;4;39msubject[0m] [[0;1;99m--raw[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh list[0m list public key identities known to the ssh agent.

      By default it prints key fingerprints, to list the raw key use the flag
      [0;1;99m--raw[0m.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39msubject[0m
          Optional subject or comment to filter keys by.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--raw[0m
          List public keys instead of fingerprints.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      List all key fingerprints known to the agent:

          $ step ssh list

      List all the key fingerprints with the comment joe@work:

          $ step ssh list joe@work

      List all keys known to the agent:

          $ step ssh list --raw

      List all the keys with the comment joe@work:

          $ step ssh list --raw joe@work

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh login[0m -- adds a SSH certificate into the authentication agent

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh login[0m [[0;4;39midentity[0m] [[0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--principal[0m=[0;4;39mstring[0m] [[0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkey-type[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m] [[0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m] [[0;1;99m--comment[0m=[0;4;39mcomment[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m] [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--console[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--force[0m] [[0;1;99m--insecure[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh login[0m generates a new SSH key pair and send a request to
      [0;1;39mstep certificates[0m to sign a user certificate. This certificate will be
      automatically added to the SSH agent.

      With a certificate servers may trust only the CA key and verify its
      signature on a certificate rather than trusting many user keys.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39midentity[0m
          The certificate identity. If no principals are passed we will use the
          identity as a principal, if it has the format abc@def then the
          principal will be abc.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--token[0m=[0;4;39mtoken[0m
          The one-time [0;4;39mtoken[0m used to authenticate with the CA in order to
          create the certificate.

      [0;1;99m--add-user[0m
          Create a user provisioner certificate used to create a new user.

      [0;1;99m--principal[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m, [0;1;99m-n[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          Add the specified principal (username) to the certificate request.
          This flag can be used multiple times. However, it cannot be used in
          conjunction with '--token' when requesting certificates from OIDC, JWK,
          and X5C provisioners, or from any provisioner with 'disableCustomSANs'
          set to 'true'. These provisioners will use the contents of the token to
          determine the principals.

      [0;1;99m--identity[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The certificate identity. It is usually passed as a positional
          argument, but a flag exists so it can be configured in
          $STEPPATH/config/defaults.json.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mname[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m, [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          one-time token generating key.

      [0;1;99m--not-before[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period starts. If
          a [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--not-after[0m=[0;4;39mtime|duration[0m
          The [0;4;39mtime|duration[0m when the certificate validity period ends. If a
          [0;4;39mtime[0m is used it is expected to be in RFC 3339 format. If a
          [0;4;39mduration[0m is used, it is a sequence of decimal numbers, each with
          optional fraction and a unit suffix, such as "300ms", "-1.5h" or
          "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or "µs"), "ms", "s", "m",
          "h".

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--console[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining inside the terminal.

      [0;1;99m-f[0m, [0;1;99m--force[0m
          Force the overwrite of files without asking.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

      [0;1;99m--comment[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The comment used when adding the certificate to an agent. Defaults to
          the subject if not provided.

      [0;1;99m--kty[0m=[0;4;39mkty[0m
          The [0;4;39mkty[0m to build the certificate upon. If unset, default is EC.

          [0;4;39mkty[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mEC[0m
              Create an [0;1;99melliptic curve[0m keypair

            [0;1;99mOKP[0m
              Create an octet key pair (for [0;1;99m"Ed25519"[0m curve)

            [0;1;99mRSA[0m
              Create an [0;1;99mRSA[0m keypair

      [0;1;99m--crv[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m, [0;1;99m--curve[0m=[0;4;39mcurve[0m
          The elliptic [0;4;39mcurve[0m to use for EC and OKP key types. Corresponds to
          the [0;1;99m"crv"[0m JWK parameter. Valid curves are defined in JWA [RFC7518].
          If unset, default is P-256 for EC keys and Ed25519 for OKP keys.

          [0;4;39mcurve[0m is a case-sensitive string and must be one of:

            [0;1;99mP-256[0m
              NIST P-256 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-384[0m
              NIST P-384 Curve

            [0;1;99mP-521[0m
              NIST P-521 Curve

            [0;1;99mEd25519[0m
              Ed25519 Curve

      [0;1;99m--size[0m=[0;4;39msize[0m
          The [0;4;39msize[0m (in bits) of the key for RSA and oct key types. RSA keys
          require a minimum key size of 2048 bits. If unset, default is 2048 bits
          for RSA keys and 128 bits for oct keys.

      [0;1;99m--insecure[0m
[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Request a new SSH certificate and add it to the agent:

          $ step ssh login bob

      Request a new SSH certificate using an OIDC provisioner:

          $ step ssh login

      Request a new SSH certificate valid only for 1h:

          $ step ssh login --not-after 1h alice

      Request a new SSH certificate with multiple principals:

          $ step ssh login --principal admin --principal bob bob@smallstep.com

      Request a new SSH certificate and set a custom comment in the agent

          $ step ssh login --comment my-custom-comment bob@smallstep.com

      Request a new SSH certificate with an EC key and P-521 curve:

          $  step ssh certificate --kty EC --curve "P-521" mariano@work id_ecdsa

      Request a new SSH certificate with an Octet Key Pair and Ed25519 curve:

          $  step ssh certificate --kty OKP --curve Ed25519 mariano@work id_ed25519

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh logout[0m -- removes a private key from the ssh-agent

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh logout[0m [[0;4;39midentity[0m] [[0;1;99m--all[0m] [[0;1;99m--identity[0m=[0;4;39midentity[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--offline[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh logout[0m commands removes a key from the ssh-agent.

      By default it only removes certificate keys signed by step-certificates,
      but the flag [0;1;99m--all[0m can be used to remove all keys with a given subject
      or all keys.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39midentity[0m
          The certificate identity or comment in the key.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--all[0m
          Removes all the keys stored in the SSH agent.

      [0;1;99m--identity[0m=[0;4;39mvalue[0m
          The certificate identity. It is usually passed as a positional
          argument, but a flag exists so it can be configured in
          $STEPPATH/config/defaults.json.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step
          path)/config/ca.json

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
          [0;4;39mURI[0m of the targeted Step Certificate Authority.

      [0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the PEM [0;4;39mfile[0m used as the root certificate authority.

      [0;1;99m--context[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The context [0;4;39mname[0m to apply for the given command.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Remove all identities signed by your SSH CA:

          $ step ssh logout

      Remove the certificate mariano@work from the SSH agent:

          $ step ssh logout mariano@work

      Remove the all the keys and certificates for mariano@work from the SSH
      agent:

          $ step ssh logout --all mariano@work

      Remove the key mariano@work from the agent listening in /tmp/ssh/agent:

          $ SSH_AUTH_SOCK=/tmp/ssh/agent step ssh logout mariano@work

      Remove all the keys stored in the SSH agent:

          $ step ssh logout --all

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh needs-renewal[0m -- Check if an SSH certificate needs to be
      renewed

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh needs-renewal[0m [0;4;39mcrt-file[0m
      [[0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mpercent|duration[0m] [[0;1;99m--verbose[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh needs-renewal[0m returns '0' if the SSH certificate needs to be
      renewed based on it's remaining lifetime. Returns '1' if the SSH
      certificate is within it's validity lifetime bounds and does not need to be
      renewed. By default, an SSH certificate "needs renewal" when it has passed
      66% (default threshold) of it's allotted lifetime. This threshold can be
      adjusted using the '--expires-in' flag.

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m
      [0;4;39mcert-file[0m
          The path to an SSH certificate.

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--expires-in[0m=[0;4;39mpercent|duration[0m
          Check if the certificate expires within the given time window using
          [0;4;39mpercent|duration[0m. If using [0;4;39mpercent[0m, the input must be followed
          by a "%" character. If using [0;4;39mduration[0m, the input must be a sequence
          of decimal numbers, each with optional fraction and a unit suffix, such
          as "300ms", "-1.5h" or "2h45m". Valid time units are "ns", "us" (or
          "µs"), "ms", "s", "m", "h".

      [0;1;99m--verbose[0m, [0;1;99m-v[0m
          Print human readable affirmation if certificate requires renewal.

[0;1;99mEXIT CODES[0m
      This command returns '0' if the SSH certificate needs renewal, '1' if the
      SSH certificate does not need renewal, '2' if the SSH certificate file does
      not exist, and '255' for any other error.

[0;1;99mEXAMPLES[0m
      Check if an SSH certificate needs renewal using the default threshold
      (66%):

          $ step ssh needs-renewal ./ssh_host_ed25519_key.pub

      Check if certificate will expire within a given duration:

          $ step ssh needs-renewal ./ssh_host_ed25519_key.pub --expires-in 1h15m

      Check if an SSH certificate has passed 75 percent of it's lifetime:

          $ step certificate needs-renewal ./ssh_host_ed25519_key.pub --expires-in 75%

[0;1;99mNAME[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh proxycommand[0m -- proxy ssh connections according to the host
      registry

[0;1;99mUSAGE[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh proxycommand[0m [0;4;39muser[0m [0;4;39mhost[0m [0;4;39mport[0m
      [[0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m] [[0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--console[0m] [[0;1;99m--offline[0m]
      [[0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m] [[0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39muri[0m] [[0;1;99m--root[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m]

[0;1;99mDESCRIPTION[0m
      [0;1;99mstep ssh proxycommand[0m looks into the host registry and proxies the ssh

[0;1;99mPOSITIONAL ARGUMENTS[0m

[0;1;99mOPTIONS[0m
      [0;1;99m--provisioner[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m, [0;1;99m--issuer[0m=[0;4;39mname[0m
          The provisioner [0;4;39mname[0m to use.

      [0;1;99m--provisioner-password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m, [0;1;99m--password-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The path to the [0;4;39mfile[0m containing the password to decrypt the
          one-time token generating key.

      [0;1;99m--set[0m=[0;4;39mkey=value[0m
          The [0;4;39mkey=value[0m pair with template data variables. Use the [0;1;99m--set[0m
          flag multiple times to add multiple variables.

      [0;1;99m--set-file[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The JSON [0;4;39mfile[0m with the template data variables.

      [0;1;99m--console[0m
          Complete the flow while remaining inside the terminal.

      [0;1;99m--offline[0m
          Creates a certificate without contacting the certificate authority.
          Offline mode uses the configuration, certificates, and keys created
          with [0;1;99mstep ca init[0m, but can accept a different configuration file
          using [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m flag.

      [0;1;99m--ca-config[0m=[0;4;39mfile[0m
          The certificate authority configuration [0;4;39mfile[0m. Defaults to $(step

      [0;1;99m--ca-url[0m=[0;4;39mURI[0m
